Number of Stones and Method of Istinja in the Hanafi School
Ruling and method on istinja with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of stones for istinja and explain the recommended wiping method, including the proofs and the differences based on anatomy.

Core Idea
Using three stones for istinja is recommended, not obligatory; the method ensures thorough cleaning without recontamination.

This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Idah clarifies the ruling on the number of stones for istinja and the detailed wiping method. The commentator explains that the command to use an odd number is interpreted as permissive, making it mandub (recommended), not an emphasized sunnah or wajib. He also provides a practical method that varies based on anatomy and gender, emphasizing thorough cleaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the number of stones
The text states that using three stones is mandatory (الثلاثة مندوب). Note the exact Arabic term: مندوب. This is the legal classification.
The matn simply says three stones; the commentator clarifies its level.
2
Understand the dalil and its implications
Two hadith are cited: one commands odd number, the other gives a choice ('whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no sin'). In Hanafi usul, the first command is overridden by the second, making the ruling mandub.
Note the phrase 'لا حرج' (no sin) is key to negating obligation.
3
Learn the recommended wiping method for a man
The method depends on whether the testicles hang down (al-khusyah mudallāh). If pendulous, wipe: first stone front-to-back, second back-to-front, third front-to-back. If not pendulous, begin back-to-front.
This order prevents recontamination of the area.
4
Learn the recommended wiping method for a woman
A woman should begin from front to back to avoid soiling her vulva.
The basis is fending off harm (dar' al-mafsadah).
5
Recognize additional sunan and the fasting case
After wiping, wash hands, then clean the area with water using fingers. Men raise middle finger first; women use middle and ring fingers together. Exaggerate in cleaning to remove smell. If fasting, dry the area before standing.
The fasting case shows consideration for the fast's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعدد في الأحجار ثلاثة مندوب، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من استجمر فليوتر» لأنه يحتمل الإباحة فيكون مندوباً، لا سنة مؤكدة؛ لأن الإنقاء هو المقصود، ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «من استجمر فليوتر، من فعل فقد أحسن، ومن لا فلا حرج»، فإنه محكم في التخيير. فيستنجي بثلاثة أحجار ندباً إن حصل التنظيف بدونها. وكيفية الاستنجاء: أن يمسح بالحجر الأول بادئاً من جهة المقدم إلى خلف، وبالثاني من خلف إلى قدام، وبالثالث من قدام إلى خلف، إذا كانت الخصية مدلاة، وإن كانت غير مدلاة يبتدئ من خلف إلى قدام. والمرأة تبتدئ من قدام إلى خلف، خشية تلويث فرجها. ثم يغسل يده أولاً بالماء، ثم يدلك المحل بالماء بباطن إصبع أو إصبعين، أو ثلاث إن احتاج. ويصعد الرجل إصبعَه الوسطى على غيرها في ابتداء الاستنجاء، ثم يصعد بنصره، ولا يقتصر على إصبع واحدة، والمرأة تصعد بنصرها وأوسط أصابعها معاً ابتداء، خشية حصول اللذة، ويبالغ في التنظيف حتى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة، وفي إرخاء المقعدة، إن لم يكن صائماً، فإذا فرغ غسل يده ثانياً، ونشف مقعدته قبل القيام، إذا كان صائماً.
And the number of stones is three, recommended, because of his saying: 'Whoever uses stones for purification should do it with an odd number' – because it admits permissibility, so it is recommended, not an emphasized sunnah, because cleansing is the purpose, and due to his saying: 'Whoever uses stones for purification should do it with an odd number; whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no sin' – for it is definitive in giving choice. So he performs istinja with three stones, as a recommendation if cleansing is achieved without them. The method of istinja: he wipes with the first stone starting from the front area towards the back, with the second from back to front, and with the third from front to back, if the testicle is pendulous. If it is not pendulous, he starts from back to front. The woman starts from front to back, fearing soiling her vulva. Then he washes his hand first with water, then rubs the area with water using the inner side of one finger, or two fingers, or three if needed. The man raises his middle finger above the others at the beginning of istinja, then raises his ring finger, and does not limit to one finger. The woman raises her ring finger and middle finger together at the beginning, fearing the occurrence of pleasure. He goes to extremes in cleaning until he removes the unpleasant smell, and in relaxing the anus, if he is not fasting. When he finishes, he washes his hand a second time, and dries his anus before standing up, if he is fasting.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the ruling on the number of stones and the detailed method of istinja. The matn states that the number of stones is three, and the commentator clarifies that this is mandub (recommended), not sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). The proof is the hadith 'whoever uses stones should do so with an odd number' which, according to Hanafi usul, indicates permissibility and thus recommendation, not obligation. The second hadith 'whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no sin' confirms the lack of obligation. The recommendation applies when cleansing is achieved without three; otherwise, one may use less. The method of wiping with stones is described in detail: the order of wiping depends on whether the testicles hang down (pendulous) – if so, first wipe from front to back, then back to front, then front to back to avoid recontamination; if not pendulous, start from back to front. Women start from front to back to avoid soiling the vulva. After wiping, one should wash the hand first, then wash the area using fingers – men start with the middle finger raised to allow water to flow down, then use other fingers; women use the ring and middle finger together to avoid pleasure. Excessive cleaning is recommended to remove smell and to relax the anus (if not fasting) to ensure complete removal. After finishing, the fasting person should wash the hand again and dry the area to protect the fast; it is also recommended for others.

Key Terms
مَنْدُوب (mandub): A recommended act; doing it is rewarded, leaving it without excuse is not sinful.
الخصية مدلاة (al-khusyah mudallāh): The testicle hanging down (pendulous), affecting the wiping order to avoid contamination.
بِنْصَر (binsir): The ring finger (the fourth finger).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using three stones for istinja according to the Hanafi school?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah)
C) Mandub (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Three stones for istinja are recommended (mandub) in the Hanafi school, not obligatory, and the wiping method should be performed in a specific order to ensure cleanliness.

Method of Istinja for Men and Women
Explains the sequence and technique of istinja with anatomical and contextual distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of istinja for men and women, distinguishing the steps based on anatomy and fasting status.

Core Idea
The method of istinja differs for men and women based on anatomy and the risk of soiling or arousal, and must be modified for the fasting person.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the practical steps of istinja (purification after relieving oneself) as taught in the Hanafi school. It provides detailed instructions tailored to the physical differences between men and women, as well as considerations for those who are fasting. Understanding these steps ensures that one's purification is both complete and legally valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the order for men based on testicle condition
If the testicles are pendulous, the man washes front to back, then back to front, then front to back. If not pendulous, he washes back to front only.
The goal is to avoid soiling the testicles.
2
Identify the order for women and the reason
Women always wash from front to back to avoid soiling the private part.
This prevents infection and impurity spread.
3
Recognize the finger usage for men and women
Men start with the middle finger, then ring finger, etc. Women use ring and middle fingers together to avoid pleasure. Virgins use the palm.
Using multiple fingers ensures thorough cleaning.
4
Understand hand-washing and drying steps
Wash hands before and after istinja. Dry the anus before standing when fasting to avoid breaking the fast.
The second hand wash removes residual impurity.
5
Apply special rules for a fasting person
Do not exaggerate in relaxing the anus or insert a wet finger, as these may break the fast.
The drying step is obligatory for fasting persons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المُقَدَّمِ إلى خلف، وبالثاني من خلف إلى قُدَّامٍ، وبالثَّالث من قدام إلى خلف، إذا كانت الخُصْيَةُ مُدَلَاةً، وإِنْ كانت غيرَ مُدَلَاةٍ، يبتدئ من خلف إلى قُدَّامِ. والمرأة تبتدئ من قُدَّامٍ إلى خَلْفِ، خَشْيَةَ تلويث فرجها. ثم يغسلُ يَدَهُ أولاً بالماء، ثم يَذلك المحل بالماء بباطن إصبع أو إصبعين، أو ثلاث إن احتاج. ويُصَعَدُ الرّجلُ إصبعَهُ الوسطى على غيرها في ابتداء الاستنجاء، ثم يصعدُ بِنصَرَهُ، ولا يقتصر على إصبع واحدة، والمرأة تصعد بِنصَرَها وأَوْسَطَ أصابعها معاً ابتداء، خشية حصولِ اللَّةِ، ويُبالغ في التنظيف حتى يقطع الرائحةَ الكَرِيهَةَ، وفي إرخاءِ المَقْعَدَةِ، إن لم يكُن صائماً، فإذا فرغ غَسَلَ بدَهُ ثَانِيَاً، ونَشْفَ مَقْعَدَتَهُ قبل القيام، إذا كان صائماً
المُقَدَّمِ) أي: القبل ( إلى خَلْفٍ، وبِالثَّانِي مِنْ خَلْفِ إلى قُدَّامِ)، ويسمى إدباراً، وبالثالث: مـن قـدام إلى خلف) وهذا الترتيب ) إِذَا كَانَتِ الخُصْيَّةُ مُدَلاًةً سواء كان صيفاً أو شتاء، خشية تلويثها، (وإنْ كَانَتْ غَيْرَ مُدَلَاةٍ، يَبْتَدِى مِنْ خَلْفِ إلى قدام)، لكونه أبلغ في التنظيف، (والمرأة تبتدى مـن قـدام إلى خَلْف، خشية تلويث فرجها ثم بعد المسح (يغسلُ يَدَهُ أوّلاً بالماء لئلا تتشرب المسام الماء النجس بـأول الاستنجاء، ثمَّ يَدْلُكُ المحلَّ بالماء بباطن إصْبَعِ، أو إصْبَعَيْنِ) في الابتداء، (أو ثــلاث إن احتاج) إليـهـا ابتداء، ويُصَعَدُ الرّجلُ إصبعَهُ الوُسْطَى عَلَى غَيْرِهَا قليلاً (فَي ابْتِدَاءِ الاسْتِنْجَاءِ)؛ لينحدر الماء النجس من غير شيوع على باقي المحل، (ثُمَّ) إذا غسل قليلاً ( يصعدُ بِنْصَرَه)، ثـم خنصره، ثم السبابة إن احتاج، ليتمكن من التنظيف، ولا يَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى إصْبَعِ واحدةٍ)؛ لأنـه يــورث داء، ولا يحصـل بـه كـمـال التنظيف. (والمَرْأةُ تُصَعَدُ بِنْصَرَهَا وأَوْسَطَ أَصَابِعِها مَعَا ابْتِدَاء خَشْيَةَ حُصُولِ اللَّـدِّةِ) لـو ابتدأت بإصبع واحدة فقد تحصل، فيجب الغسل عليها ولا تشعر. والعذراء لا تستنجي بأصابعها بـل بـراحـة كفـهـا، خوفاً من زوال العذرة ). (ويبالغ) المستنجي ( في التنظيف، حتّى يقطع الرائحة الكريهة ) ولم يُقَدِّره بعدد؛ لأن الصحيح تفويضه إلى رأيه، حتى يطمئن قلبه أنه قد طهر بيقين، أو غلبة الظن، ولا يقدر بالعدد إلا أن يكون موسوساً، فيقدر بالثلاث في حقه، وقيل: بالسبع، وقيل: يقدر في الإحليل) بالثلاث، وفي المقعدة بالخمس، وقيل: بالتسع، وقيل: بالعشر، (و) يبالغ (في إرخاء المقعدة)؛ ليزيل ما في الشرج بقدر الإمكان ( إن لم يكن صائماً)، فإن كان صائماً لا يبالغ، حذراً من إفساد الصوم، ويحترز أيضاً من إدخال الإصبع مبتلة، فإنه يفسد الصوم، (فَإِذَا فَرَغَ) من الاستنجاء بالماء (غَسَلَ يَدَهُ ثانِيَاً، ونَشَّفَ مَقْعَدَتَهُ قبل القيام)؛ لئلا تجذب المقعدة شيئاً من الماء ( إذَا كَانَ صَائِمَاً)، ويستحب لـغـيـر الصائم أيضاً حفظاً للثوب عن الماء المستعمل.
From the front to the back, and with the second from the back to the front, and with the third from the front to the back, if the testicle is pendulous; and if it is not pendulous, he begins from the back to the front. The woman begins from the front to the back, fearing soiling her private part. Then he washes his hand first with water, then rubs the place with water using the inside of one finger, or two, or three if needed. The man elevates his middle finger over others at the beginning of istinja, then elevates his ring finger, and does not restrict to one finger. The woman elevates her ring finger and middle finger together initially, fearing pleasure. And he exaggerates in cleaning until he removes the bad smell, and in relaxing the anus if he is not fasting; then when he finishes, he washes his hand a second time, and dries his anus before standing if he is fasting.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the method of istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself) as prescribed in the Hanafi school. It begins by describing the order of washing for a man: if the testicles are pendulous, he washes from front to back, then back to front, then front to back again to prevent soiling them. If not pendulous, he starts from back to front for better cleaning. A woman always starts from front to back to avoid soiling her private part. After wiping, he washes his hand first to prevent the pores from absorbing impure water. Then he rubs the area with one, two, or three fingers as needed. The man should use his middle finger initially, then ring finger, then little finger, then index finger if needed—never just one finger, as that causes disease and incomplete cleaning. The woman uses her ring and middle fingers together to avoid pleasure; if she used one finger, she might become aroused and require a ritual bath unknowingly. A virgin should not use her fingers but the palm of her hand to avoid breaking the hymen. The person should exaggerate cleaning until the bad smell is removed, without a fixed number of washes; the correct view is to rely on his judgment until certain or strongly confident of purity, except for a waswasi (obsessive) who should limit to three (or seven, or for the urethra three, anus five, nine, or ten). He should also relax the anus to expel residue, but not if fasting, as it might break the fast. He must also avoid inserting a wet finger, as that invalidates the fast. After finishing, he washes his hand a second time and dries his anus before standing, recommended for non-fasting persons as well to protect clothing from used water.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinjā’): The act of cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, typically with water or stones.
الخصية المدلاة (al-khuṣyah al-mudalāh): A pendulous testicle that hangs down, requiring a specific washing order to avoid soiling.
العذراء (al-ʿadhrā’): A virgin woman who has not had intercourse; she should not use her fingers for istinja but the palm of her hand to protect the hymen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) To protect the hymen

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of istinja is detailed and takes into account anatomy, fasting, and the risk of impurity spread or arousal.

Ruling on Exposing Awrah for Istinja and Najasah Exceeding a Dirham
States the ruling on exposing awrah and the condition for najasah exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that exposing the 'awrah for istinja is absolutely prohibited and identify the condition under which najasah exceeding a dirham invalidates prayer.

Core Idea
Exposing awrah is haram even for istinja; najasah beyond a dirham invalidates prayer if removable.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary explains two interconnected rulings: the absolute prohibition of exposing the private parts even for cleaning, and the threshold for impurity that nullifies prayer. Understanding these rulings is crucial for maintaining valid prayer while avoiding sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states 'لا يجوز كشف العورة للاستنجاء' – it is not permissible to expose the 'awrah for istinja. This is the primary ruling to note.
2
Determine the hukm level
The commentary clarifies that exposing the 'awrah is haram (forbidden) and makes one sinful. The phrase 'حرام يفسق به' indicates it is a major sin.
Hukm level: haram.
3
Understand the practical consequence for istinja
Since istinja is sunnah (not fard), one must perform it without exposing the 'awrah. The text suggests using stones or similar under the clothes.
Istinja is sunnah; avoiding haram takes precedence.
4
Identify the condition for najasah exemption
The passage discusses najasah that exceeds the exit. The amount inside the exit is disregarded. Only the spread portion is considered. If that spread exceeds a dirham, prayer is invalid, provided something is available to remove it.
Dirham measure: weight for solids, area for liquids.
5
Note the removal requirement
The invalidity of prayer is conditional on the availability of something (water or liquid) to remove the najasah. If unavailable, the prayer may be valid with the impurity.
If no water, the ruling may change; seek detailed fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يجوز به الاستنجاء

لا يجوزُ كشف العورة للاستِنْجَاءِ، وإنْ تجاوزتِ النَّجاسَةُ مخرجها، وزادَ المُتَجاوِزُ على قَدْرِ الدّرهم، لا تصح مَعَهُ الصَّلاةُ، إذا وُجِدَ ما يُزيلُهُ ، ويحتالُ لإزالتِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ كشف العورة عند من يراه.

فصل فيما يجوز به الاستنجاء، وما يكره به، وما يكره فعله

( لا يَجُوزُ كَشْفُ العَوْرِةِ للاستِنْجَاءِ) عند من يراه؛ لأن كشفها حرام يفسق بـه، ولـو كـان عـلـى شط نهر لا سترة فيه، فلا يرتكب المحرم، لإقامة السنة). ويزيل ما في المخرج بنحـو حـجـر مـن تحت ثيابه، وتصح الصلاة بدون الاستنجاء، لكونه سنة إذا لم تتجاوز مخرجها، (وإن تجاوزت النَّجاسة مخرجها قيد به، لأن ما في المخرج ساقط الاعتبار، ولا يضم ذلك إلى ما يبلغ قدر الدرهم به من المتجاوز، فلا يمنعان صحة الصلاة، (وَ) إذا زَادَ المُتَجاوِزُ) بانفراده (عَلَى قَدْرِ الدّرهم) وزناً في المتجسدة، ومساحة في المائعة، لا تَصِحُ مَعَهُ الصَّلاةُ)؛ لزيادته عـلـى القـدر المعفو عنه ( إذا وجد ما يُزيلُهُ) من ماء أو مائع، (وَيَحْتَالُ لإِزَالَتِهِ، مِنْ غَيْرِ كَشْفِ العَوْرَةِ عِنْدَ مَنْ يَرَاهُ)، تحرزاً عن ارتكاب المحرم بالقدر الممكن.
Chapter on what is permissible for istinja

It is not permissible to expose the private parts for istinja, and if the impurity exceeds its exit and the amount exceeding the size of a dirham, prayer is not valid with it, if something is found to remove it, and one should contrive to remove it without exposing the private parts in the presence of one who sees him.

Chapter on what is permissible for istinja, what is disliked for it, and what is disliked to do

(It is not permissible to expose the private parts for istinja) in the presence of one who sees him, because exposing them is forbidden and makes one sinful; even if he is on the bank of a river without cover, he should not commit the forbidden in order to perform the sunnah. And he removes what is in the exit with something like a stone from under his clothes, and prayer is valid without istinja because it is sunnah if the impurity does not exceed its exit. (And if the impurity exceeds its exit) it is restricted because what is in the exit is disregarded, and that is not added to what reaches the size of a dirham from the exceeding amount, so they do not prevent the validity of prayer. (And) if the exceeding amount (by itself) exceeds the size of a dirham by weight in solids, and by area in liquids, prayer is not valid with it due to its exceeding the pardoned amount, (if something is found to remove it) of water or liquid. (And one contrives to remove it without exposing the private parts in the presence of one who sees him) to avoid committing the forbidden as much as possible.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn and its commentary. It establishes that exposing the 'awrah (private parts) is absolutely prohibited, even for the purpose of istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself). The prohibition remains even if one is on a riverbank with no cover. Instead, one should clean the exit from under one's clothes using stones or similar objects. Istinja itself is sunnah, not obligatory; therefore, prayer is valid without it if the impurity does not spread beyond the exit. The passage then discusses the exemption for najasah (impurity) that spreads. If the impurity exceeds the exit, the portion inside the exit is disregarded. Only the amount that spreads outside is considered. If that amount is less than the size of a dirham, it is pardoned and prayer is valid. If it equals or exceeds a dirham, prayer is not valid provided something (water or liquid) is available to remove it. In such a case, one must contrive to remove it without exposing the 'awrah. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that avoiding a forbidden act takes precedence over performing a sunnah act.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): The act of cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, typically using water or stones.
العورة (al-'awrah): The private parts that must be covered; for men, the area between navel and knees; for women, the entire body except face and hands in prayer.
النجاسة (al-najasah): Impurity, specifically here refers to urine or feces that exits the body.
الدرهم (al-dirham): A silver coin; used as a measure of area (approximately the size of a fingertip) or weight in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following statements is correct according to the Hanafi school?
A) Exposing awrah for istinja is permissible if no one sees.
B) Istinja is obligatory for prayer to be valid.
C) Najasah that spreads beyond the exit and exceeds a dirham invalidates prayer if removable.
D) The amount of najasah inside the exit is counted towards the dirham threshold.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits exposing awrah for istinja absolutely, and prayer is invalid if najasah exceeding a dirham is present and removable.

Disliked Materials for Istinja in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists and explains materials disliked for istinja with reasons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the materials disliked for istinja according to the Hanafi school and explain the reasoning (dalil and illa) behind each prohibition.

Core Idea
Istinja with bone, dung, food, or valuable items is disliked because it disrespects jinn provision, wastes resources, or harms the body.

Istinja (cleaning after relieving oneself) is a key act of purification. While water or stones are recommended, certain materials are disliked. This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling on which materials are makruh and why, based on the hadith forbidding bone and dung and analogical reasoning for other items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Istinja itself is sunnah (recommended) in the Hanafi school. The lesson focuses on materials that are makruh (disliked) for this act. Note that makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) applies to bone and dung, while makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) applies to others.
The hadith uses a negative imperative (la tastanju), which Hanafi usul interprets as indicating karahah tahrimiyyah.
2
List the seven disliked materials from the text
The matn lists: bone, food (human or animal), baked brick (ajur), and pottery (khazaf). The commentary adds: dung, charcoal, glass, plaster, valuable items (brocade, cotton), and use of the right hand without excuse.
Dung and bone are the primary items; others are added via qiyas (analogy) based on similar illa (effective cause).
3
Understand the dalil for bone and dung
The Prophet (pbuh) said: 'Do not perform istinja with dung or bones, for they are the provision of your brothers among the jinn.' This hadith is reported in multiple collections. The prohibition is because these items are food for the jinn, and using them disrespects that.
The hadith is ahad (solitary) but its meaning is clear; Hanafi usul treats it as zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah.
4
Apply the reasoning for other items
Food (human or animal) is disliked due to waste and disrespect. Hard items (baked brick, pottery, glass, plaster) harm the body or fail to clean properly. Valuable items (silk, cotton) waste wealth. Charcoal soils. Use of right hand is disliked except for an excuse.
The general principle is avoiding waste (israf), harm (idha'), or disrespect (ihana).
5
Note the exception and etiquette
Using the right hand is only permissible if there is an excuse (e.g., left hand injured). Performing istinja with water should be done with flowing water or with help from a servant/spouse to avoid splashing impurity.
This reflects the comprehensive Hanafi attention to both ritual purity and practical adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكره الاستنجاء بعظم، وطعام لآدمي، أو بهيمةٍ، وآجر، وخَزَف .

ويُكره الاستنجاء: بَعَظم) وروث؛ لقولـه عليـه الصـلاة والسلام: لا تَسْتَنْجُوا بِالرَّوْثِ، وَلَا بِالْعِظَامِ، فَإِنَّهُمَا زَادُ إِخْوَانِكُمْ مِنْ الْجِنِّ). وفي « دلائل النبوة» للحافظ أبي نعيم، أن الجن التمسوا منه ليلة الجن هدية، فأعطاهم العظم والروث. فإذا وجدوهمـا صـار العظم كأن لم يؤكل، فيأكلونه، وصار الــروث شعيراً وتبنـا وعـلفـاً آخر لدوابهم، وذلك معجزة للنبي ، بتعليمه تعالى إياه، والنهي يقتضي كراهة التحريم (وَطَعَامِ لَآ دَمِي، أَوْ بَهِيمَةٍ)؛ للإسراف والإهانة وإتلاف المال، وقد نهى عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام (۳) (وآجر) بمـد الهمزة، وضم الجيم، وتشديد الراء المهملة، فارسي مُعَرَّب، وهو : الطوب، بلغة أهل مصر. ويقال له: أجور على وزن فاعول: اللبن المحرق، كره به لخشونته، فلا ينقي المحل ويؤذيه، وخَزَف) هــو : صغار الحصى؛ لعدم التمكن من الإنقاء بها، وقد تلوث يده، (وَفَحْم) لتلويثه (وزُجاج، وحص)؛ لأنه يضر المحل (وشيءٍ مُحترم) لتقومه (كخِرقةٍ ديباج، وقُطن)؛ لإتلاف المالية والاستنجاء بـهـا يــورث الفقر. (و) يكره الاستنجاء بِاليَدِ اليُمْنَى) لما روى أصحاب الكتب الستة عن أبي قتادة، قال: قــال رســول الله : ( إِذَا بَالَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلا يَمْسَحْ ذَكَرَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ، وَإِذَا أَتَى الْخَلاء فَلا يَتَمَسَّحْ بِيَمِينِهِ، وَإِذَا شَرِبَ فَلا يَشْرَبْ نَفَسًا وَاحِدًا ) ( إلا مِنْ عُدْرٍ) باليسرى يمنع الاستنجاء بها، فلا يكره الاستنجاء بيمينه. وإذا استنجى بالماء يكون على شط ماء جار أو بصب خادم أو زوجته.
And istinja is disliked with bone, and food for human or animal, and baked brick, and small stones.

And istinja is disliked with bone and dung; because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not perform istinja with dung or bones, for they are the provision of your brothers among the jinn.' And in 'Dala'il al-Nubuwwa' by al-Hafiz Abu Nu'aym, that the jinn asked him on the night of the jinn for a gift, so he gave them bone and dung. When they find them, the bone becomes as if it had not been eaten, so they eat it, and the dung becomes barley, hay, and other fodder for their animals, and that is a miracle of the Prophet, taught by Allah. And the prohibition indicates dislikedness close to prohibition. And food for human or animal due to waste, disrespect, and waste of wealth, and the Prophet forbade it. And 'ajur (baked brick) is a Persian word arabicized, meaning baked brick in Egyptian dialect, also called 'ajur on the pattern of fa'ul. It is disliked because of its roughness, so it does not clean properly and harms. And khazaf (pottery) is small pebbles; because it is not possible to clean well with them and they soil the hand. And charcoal because it dirties, and glass and plaster because they harm the body. And something valuable because it is property, like a piece of brocade or cotton; because it destroys wealth and istinja with it brings poverty. And istinja with the right hand is disliked due to the hadith narrated by the authors of the six books from Abu Qatada: the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you urinates, let him not wipe his penis with his right hand; and when he goes to the lavatory, let him not wipe himself with his right hand; and when he drinks, let him not drink in one breath.' Except due to an excuse in the left hand preventing istinja, then it is not disliked. And if one performs istinja with water, it should be on the bank of a flowing river or by a servant or his wife pouring water.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof (hadith) explaining the materials and actions disliked (makruh) in istinja. The matn lists bone, human or animal food, baked brick (ajur), and pottery (khazaf). The commentary expands the list with dung, charcoal, glass, plaster, valuable items like brocade or cotton, and the use of the right hand. The prohibition for bone and dung is from a hadith: they are provision for the jinn. For food, it is wasteful and disrespectful. For hard or valuable items, they either harm, don't clean well, or waste property. Using the right hand is disliked as per hadith, except for an excuse. The Hanafi ruling is that these are makruh tahrimi or tanzihi depending on the item; the hadith indicates makruh tahrimi for bone and dung. The passage also notes the etiquette of using water from a flowing source or servant. This teaches comprehensive fiqh of istinja, balancing purity, prohibition, and respect for food and property.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, the main act under discussion.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action for which there is reward for leaving and no sin for doing, but the stronger prohibition (tahrimi) indicates sin.
الروث (al-rawth): Dung of animals, specifically here that of horses or similar, used as a material for istinja.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are impure and spread najasah
B) The Prophet forbade it because they are food for the jinn
C) They are too hard and harm the body
D) They are not readily available

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits istinja with bone and dung due to a clear hadith; other materials are disliked due to waste, harm, or disrespect.

Etiquette of Entering the Lavatory
Ruling on lavatory etiquettes with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan actions for entering the lavatory and identify the proofs from the hadith cited.

Core Idea
Entering with the left foot and reciting basmalah and ta'awwudh screens from the jinn.

This lesson details the recommended adab (etiquettes) when entering the lavatory. These actions are sunnah muakkadah, established by sound hadiths. Understanding them helps us practice the Sunnah even in the most private moments, combining physical action with spiritual protection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is entering the lavatory. The text presents it as a recommended practice, so its hukm level is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
2
Extract the prescribed actions
From the text, list the specific sunan: enter with the left foot, recite basmalah, recite ta'awwudh (A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim), and cover the head (implied by 'istiḥbāb'). Also note the order: basmalah before ta'awwudh.
The text explicitly states 'yuqaddimu tasmiyata Allah ta'ala 'ala al-isti'adha.'
3
Link each action to its proof
The two hadiths cited: 'The screen between the eyes of the jinn and the private parts is to say Bismillah' and 'The toilets are inhabited, so say A'udhu billahi min al-khubuthi wa al-khaba'ith.' These prove the sunnah of saying both.
The first hadith is the main proof for basmalah; the second for ta'awwudh.
4
Understand the linguistic background
The commentary explains 'shaytan' and 'rajim'. Recognize that shaytan includes rebellious jinn and humans, and 'rajim' means stoned with curse or one who stones with misguidance.
This enriches the spiritual significance of seeking refuge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدخل الخلاء برجله اليُسرى، ويستعيذُ بالله منَ الشَّيطان الرجيم قبلَ دُخُولِهِ، وقبل كشف عورته، ويقدم تسميه الله تعالى على الاستعاذة؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «سِتْرُ مَا بَيْنَ أَعْيُنِ الْجِنِّ وَعَوْرَاتِ بَنِي آدَمَ، إِذَا دَخَلَ أَحَدُكُمُ الخَلاءَ أَنْ يَقُولَ: بِسم الله ) (۳). رواه عليه. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( إنَّ الحشوش مُحْتَضَرَةٌ، فإذا أتى أحدكم الخَلاءَ فليقل: أعوذ بالله من الخبث والخَبَائِثِ ). والشيطان معروف، وهو من شَطَنَ يَشْطُن إذا بعد، ويقال فيه: شاطن وشَيْطَن، ويسمى بذلك كل متمرد من الجن والإنس والدواب لبعد غوره في الشر ) . وقيل : من شَاط يشيط، إذا هلك، فالمتمرد هالك بتمرده، ويجوز أن يكون مسمى بفعلان لمبالغته في إهلاك غيره. والشياطين على ضربين: جني وإنسي، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَا لِكُلِّ نَبِي عَدُوا شَيَاطِينَ الْإِنسِ وَالْجِنَ) [الانعت : ۱۱۲]. والرجيم، بمعنى المرجوم بالطرد واللعن، وقيل: هو بمعنى فاعل: أي: يرجم غيره بالإغواء.
And he enters the lavatory with his left foot, and seeks refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan before entering, and before exposing his private parts, and he gives precedence to saying the name of Allah over seeking refuge; due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The screen between the eyes of the jinn and the private parts of the children of Adam, when one of you enters the lavatory, is to say: Bismillah.' And due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, the toilets are inhabited, so when one of you comes to the lavatory, let him say: A'udhu billahi min al-khubuthi wa al-khaba'ith.' And shaytan is known, and it is from shatana yashṭunu meaning he became distant, and it is said: shāṭin and shayṭān, and every rebellious one from jinn, humans, and animals is called by that due to the depth of his evil. And it is said: from shāṭa yashīṭu meaning he perished, so the rebellious one is perished by his rebellion. And it is possible that it is derived from fa'lān due to his exaggeration in causing others to perish. And the devils are of two types: jinn and human. Allah said: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy—devils from mankind and jinn.' And 'rajim' means the one who is stoned with expulsion and curse, and it is said: it means an active participle: i.e., one who stones others with misguidance.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the adab (etiquette) of entering the lavatory. It instructs to enter with the left foot (as a sign of honor for the right foot, since the lavatory is an unclean place), to cover the head (istiḥbāb), and to seek refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan before entering and before exposing the 'awrah. The basmalah is to be said before the ta'awwudh. The proof is the hadith: 'The screen between the eyes of the jinn and the private parts of the children of Adam...' and another hadith: 'The toilets are inhabited...' The commentary then explains the etymology of shaytan, stating that it refers to any rebellious being from jinn, humans, or animals due to the depth of its evil, or from the root meaning to perish. It also mentions the two types of shayatin: jinn and ins (humans), citing Quran 6:112. 'Rajim' means stoned with expulsion and curse, or one who stoned others with misguidance. This passage teaches both the practical etiquette and the spiritual dimension of remembering Allah in places where the devil is present.

Key Terms
الخَلاء (al-khala): The place for relieving oneself; lavatory or toilet.
الاستعاذة (al-isti'adha): Seeking refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan, specifically the phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'.
الشيطان (al-shaytan): The devil; any rebellious being from jinn, humans, or animals that leads astray.

Key Takeaway

Disliked Materials and Using Right Hand for Istinja
Ruling on disliked materials and hand for istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which materials are makruh for istinja and explain why using the right hand is disliked, including the exception for an excuse.

Core Idea
Istinja with valuable materials or the right hand is makruh; the rule honors property and cleanliness.

This lesson examines items and actions that are disliked (makruh) when performing istinja (cleansing after relieving). The text lists specific materials like charcoal, glass, plaster, and anything valuable (e.g., silk, cotton), and also prohibits using the right hand. However, an excuse (e.g., injury to the left hand) permits using the right hand. The ruling is supported by a prophetic hadith. Understanding these restrictions helps preserve property and follow Prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and its legal classification (hukm). Here, the act is performing istinja with certain materials or with the right hand, and the ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text uses 'يكره' repeatedly.
2
List the Disliked Materials
Extract the specific items mentioned: charcoal (فحم), glass (زجاج), plaster (جص), and anything valuable (محترم) like silk cloth and cotton. Understand the reasoning given: charcoal dirties, glass/plaster harm, valuable items waste property.
3
Examine the Right Hand Ruling
Note that using the right hand for istinja is makruh. Then identify the exception: an excuse (e.g., left hand is injured or unable to clean).
The hadith prohibits wiping with the right hand, but the exception overrides the prohibition.
4
Analyze the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is a hadith from Abu Qatada: the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited wiping with the right hand. In Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) indicates karahah (dislike) unless there is evidence for tahrim. Here, no such evidence, so it is makruh tanzihi.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), so its thubut is zanni.
5
Apply the Exception
Understand that if the left hand cannot be used (due to injury, etc.), then using the right hand is not disliked. The same applies if water is poured by a servant or wife to avoid touching.
The exception shows the ruling is non-absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفحم، وزجاج، وجص، وشيء مُحْتَرَم كخِرقةٍ دِيباج، وقطن، وباليد اليمنى، إلا منْ عُذر. لعدم التمكن من الإنقاء بها، وقد تلوث يده، (وَفَحْم) لتلويثه (وزُجاج، وحص)؛ لأنه يضر المحل (وشيءٍ محترم) لتقومه (كخِرقةٍ ديباج، وقُطن)؛ لإتلاف المالية والاستنجاء بها يورث الفقر. (و) يكره الاستنجاء بِاليَدِ اليُمْنَى) لما روى أصحاب الكتب الستة عن أبي قتادة، قال: قال رسول الله : ( إِذَا بَالَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلا يَمْسَحْ ذَكَرَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ، وَإِذَا أَتَى الْخَلاء فَلا يَتَمَسَّحُ بِيَمِينِهِ، وَإِذَا شَرِبَ فَلا يَشْرَبْ نَفَسًا وَاحِدًا ) ( إلا مِنْ عُدْرٍ) باليسرى يمنع الاستنجاء بها، فلا يكره الاستنجاء بيمينه. وإذا استنجى بالماء يكون على شط ماء جار أو بصب خادم أو زوجته.
And charcoal, glass, plaster, and something valuable like a silk cloth, and cotton, and with the right hand, except for an excuse. Because of inability to clean with it, and his hand may have become dirty. (And charcoal) because it dirties; (and glass, and plaster) because they harm the place; (and something valuable) because of its value (like a silk cloth and cotton) because of wasting property and istinja with it causes poverty. (And) it is disliked to perform istinja with the right hand, as narrated by the authors of the six books from Abu Qatada: the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you urinates, let him not wipe his penis with his right hand; when he goes to the toilet, let him not wipe with his right hand; and when he drinks, let him not drink in one breath.' (Except for an excuse) with the left hand preventing istinja with it, then istinja with the right hand is not disliked. And if he performs istinja with water, he should be on the bank of flowing water or by pouring from a servant or his wife.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith. It lists items that are makruh (disliked) to use for istinja: charcoal (because it dirties), glass and plaster (because they harm the private area), and anything valuable like silk cloth or cotton (because it wastes wealth, and istinja with them may cause poverty). It then states it is makruh to use the right hand for istinja, citing the hadith of Abu Qatada (radiyallahu anhu) which prohibits wiping with the right hand. The exception is if there is an excuse, such as the left hand being injured or unable to perform istinja, in which case using the right hand is not disliked. Additionally, if one uses water for istinja, it is recommended to be on a bank of flowing water or to have water poured by a servant or wife to avoid using the right hand.

Key Terms
استنجاء (istinja'): Cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself, whether with water or stones/solid matter.
محترم (muhtaram): Something valuable, the waste of which is prohibited (like silk or cotton cloth).
يمين (yamin): The right hand, used for honorable acts; using it for istinja is disliked.

Etiquettes of Entering the Toilet
Rules for entering the toilet: foot, du'a, sitting, silence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended etiquettes for entering the toilet, cite the relevant hadith proofs, and distinguish between sunnah and makruh actions in this context.

Core Idea
Entering with left foot, covering head, and reciting Bismillah and A'udhu are recommended for protection; speaking without need is disliked.

This passage from Nur al-Idah details the proper conduct when entering the place of relieving oneself. These actions are not obligatory but are strongly recommended to follow the Sunnah and seek protection from shayateen. Understanding these etiquettes helps a Muslim maintain modesty and mindfulness even in private moments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
List the actions mentioned: entering with the left foot, covering the head, saying Bismillah and A'udhu before entering, sitting leaning on the left side with the right foot erect, and avoiding speech.
These are all from the sunnah.
2
Determine the ruling level for each
All these actions are sunnah (recommended). Speaking without necessity is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
The hadith indicate recommendation, not obligation.
3
Examine the proofs cited
Two hadith are quoted: the first about Bismillah being a screen between jinn and private parts, and the second about the lavatories being frequented by devils, so one should say A'udhu. Also, a hadith about Allah detesting talking while on the toilet.
These are ahad hadith, but accepted for amal.
4
Understand the wisdom
The right foot is honored; the left is used for dirty places. Covering the head and seeking refuge protect from shayateen. Silence avoids Allah's displeasure and maintains modesty.
Etiquettes aim to spiritual and physical well-being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَدْخُلُ الخَلاءَ) قال الجوهري: الخلاء ممدود المتوضأ، والخلاء أيضاً: المكان الذي لا شيء فيه. انتهى. والمراد بيت التغوط، يدخله مريد الطهارة ( برجله اليُسرى ابتداء مستور الرأس استحباباً، تكرمة لليمني، لأن الخلاء موضع مستقذر ، يحضره الشيطان (وَيَسْتَعِيْدُ) أي: يعتصم. قال في « المصباح» : استعذت بالله، وعذت به معاذاً وعياذاً، اعتصمت بالله منَ الشَّيطان الرجيم قبلَ دُخُولِهِ) وقبل كشف عورته، ويقدم تسميه الله تعالى على الاستعاذة؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «سِتْرُ مَا بَيْنَ أَعْيُنِ الْجِنِّ وَعَوْرَاتِ بَنِي آدَمَ، إِذَا دَخَلَ أَحَدُكُمُ الخَلاءَ أَنْ يَقُولَ: بِسم الله ) (۳). رواه عليه. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( إنَّ الحشوش مُحْتَضَرَةٌ، فإذا أتى أحدكم الخَلاءَ فليقل: أعوذ بالله من الخبث والخَبَائِثِ ). والشيطان معروف، وهو من شَطَنَ يَشْطُن إذا بعد، ويقال فيه: شاطن وشَيْطَن، ويسمى بذلك كل متمرد من الجن والإنس والدواب لبعد غوره في الشر ) . وقيل : من شَاط يشيط، إذا هلك، فالمتمرد هالك بتمرده، ويجوز أن يكون مسمى بفعلان لمبالغته في إهلاك غيره. والشياطين على ضربين: جني وإنسي، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَا لِكُلِّ نَبِي عَدُوا شَيَاطِينَ الْإِنسِ وَالْجِنَ) [الأنعام: ۱۱۲]. والرجيم، بمعنى المرجوم بالطرد واللعن، وقيل: هو بمعنى فاعل: أي: يرجم غيره بالإغواء. ويجلس مُعتمداً على يسَارِهِ) من رجليه ناصباً اليمنى منهما، بأن يضع أصابعها على الأرض، ويرفع باقيها لأن ذلك أسهل لخروج الخارج ولأنه المناسب هنا، ويوسع فيما بين رجليه، ولا يتكلّم، إلا لضرورة) فإن الله يمقت على ذلك، قال : « لا يَخْرُجُ الرَّجُلانِ يَضْرِبَانِ الْغَائِطَ كَاشِفَيْنِ عَنْ عَوْرَتِهِمَا، يَتَحَدَّثَانِ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ يَمْقُتُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ ).
And he enters the toilet - al-Jawhari said: 'al-khala' with elongation is the place for ablution; also a place with nothing in it.' End. What is meant is the house of defecation; the one intending purification enters it (with his left foot initially, covering his head, as a recommendation, honoring the right, because the toilet is a dirty place frequented by the shaytan). (And he seeks refuge) meaning: he seeks protection. In al-Misbah: 'ista'dhtu billah' etc. (from the accursed shaytan before entering) and before uncovering his private parts, and he precedes the name of Allah over the seeking refuge; due to his statement (sallallahu alayhi wasallam): 'The screen between the eyes of the jinn and the private parts of the children of Adam, when one of you enters the toilet, is that he says: Bismillah.' And due to his statement: 'The lavatories are frequented, so when one of you goes to the toilet, let him say: A'udhu billah from the male and female devils.' And shaytan is known, derived from shatana meaning to be distant; each rebellious one among jinn, humans, and animals is called shaytan due to deep evil. It is also said from shata meaning to perish. Shayateen are of two types: jinn and human. Allah says: 'And thus we made for every prophet an enemy, shayateen of mankind and jinn' (al-An'am 112). Al-rajim means the one stoned with expulsion and curse. (And he sits leaning on his left side) of his legs, erecting the right one, placing its toes on the ground and raising the rest, because that is easier for the exit of excrement and because it is appropriate here, and he widens between his legs, (and does not speak, except for necessity) for Allah detests that. He said: 'Two men should not go out to defecate uncovering their private parts and talking, for Allah detests that.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage details the etiquettes of entering the toilet (al-khala'). It is recommended (mustahab) to enter with the left foot first, covering the head as a sign of respect for the right foot, because the toilet is a filthy place frequented by shayateen. One should seek refuge (isti'adha) with Allah before entering and before uncovering the private parts, and it is better to say 'Bismillah' before 'A'udhu'. The author cites a hadith that the screen between jinn and human private parts is saying 'Bismillah', and also the hadith 'The lavatories are frequented, so say A'udhu billah from male and female devils.' The passage then discusses the etymology of shaytan and rajim. Then it describes the sitting posture: leaning on the left side, right foot erect with toes on the ground, and legs spread apart to facilitate elimination. It is disliked to speak unless necessary, based on the hadith that Allah detests two men talking while defecating.

Key Terms
خلاء (khala'): The toilet or place of relieving oneself, also a vacant place.
استعاذة (isti'adha): Seeking refuge with Allah from the accursed shaytan.
حشوش (hushush): Places of defecation; originally date palm groves where people used to relieve themselves.
مقت (muqt): Intense hatred or detestation from Allah.

Facing the Qibla During Elimination: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istinja
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on facing and turning one's back to the qibla during elimination, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding istinja.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla during elimination is strictly disliked; cleaning after is disputed by al-Tamurtashi.

Facing the qibla while relieving oneself is a serious matter in Hanafi fiqh, classified as makruh tahrimi. This lesson explains the ruling, its proof from the hadith, and a notable intra-Hanafi difference concerning facing the qibla during istinja (cleaning). Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary sin and applies the school's detailed methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Note that the act is facing the qibla with the private parts during elimination, and the ruling is makruh tahrimi (strictly disliked). The same applies to turning one's back.
The text explicitly uses 'يكره تحريماً'.
2
Locate the dalil and its generality
The hadith 'When you go to defecate, do not face the qibla nor turn your backs...' is the proof. It is general, covering both open spaces and buildings, as the text emphasises with 'ولو في البنيان'.
This generality is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Notice the intra-Hanafi dispute on istinja
The text records that scholars differed regarding facing the qibla during istinja (cleaning after elimination). Al-Tamurtashi chose it is not makruh, implying a lenient view within the school.
The opposing dalil is not given but likely based on limiting the hadith to the act of elimination.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: For a person performing istinja, the general view holds it makruh to face qibla; Tamurtashi's choice permits it.
This affects daily practice for many.
5
Note the recommended action if forgetful
If someone inadvertently faces the qibla and remembers, it is mustahab to turn away, based on a hadith promising forgiveness.
This shows the school's emphasis on reverence even after a lapse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكْرَهُ تَحْرِيمَاً : اسْتِقْبَالُ القِبلَةِ بالفرج حال قضاء الحاجة. واختلفوا في الاستقبال للتطهير، واختار « التمرتاشي» أنه لا يكره (و) يكره ( اسْتِدْبَارُهَا ) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إذا أتَيْتُمُ الْغَائِطِ، فَلا تَسْتَقْبِلُوا الْقِبْلَةَ، وَلا تَسْتَدْبِرُوهَا، وَلَكِنْ شَرِّقُوا أَوْ غَرُوبُوا . وهو بإطلاقه يتناول البناء والفضاء، فلذا قال: (وَلَو) في البُنْيَانِ) وإذا جلس مستقبلاً ناسياً، فتذكر، يستحب له الانحراف بقدر ما يمكنه. لما أخرجه الطبري مرفوعاً: «مَنْ جَلَسَ يُبولُ قبالة القبلة، فانْحَرَفَ عَنْهَا إجلالاً لهَا، لَمْ يقُمْ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ حَتَّى يُغْفَرُ لَهُ ).
And it is strictly disliked (makruh tahrimi) facing the qibla with the private part during elimination. And they differed regarding facing the qibla for istinja (cleaning), and al-Tamurtashi chose that it is not disliked. (And) it is disliked to turn one's back to it, due to his statement (sallallahu alayhi wasallam): 'When you go to defecate, do not face the qibla nor turn your backs to it, but face east or west.' And its generality includes buildings and open spaces, so he said: (wow) in the building. And if someone sits facing it forgetfully, then remembers, it is recommended for him to turn away as much as possible, as narrated by al-Tabari marfu'an: 'Whoever sits to urinate facing the qibla, then turns away from it out of reverence, he will not leave his place until he is forgiven.'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is makruh tahrimi (strictly disapproved) to face the qibla with one's private parts during elimination (urination or defecation), and likewise to turn one's back to the qibla. This is based on the hadith: 'When you go to the lavatory, do not face the qibla nor turn your backs to it, but face east or west.' The Hanafi school applies this ruling even when inside a building, as indicated by the commentary. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding facing the qibla during istinja (cleaning with water) after elimination. Al-Tamurtashi chose that it is not makruh. If someone inadvertently faces the qibla and remembers, it is recommended (mustahab) to turn away, as per the hadith that one who turns away out of reverence will be forgiven before leaving.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca, faced during prayer.
تحريماً (tahriman): Strictly disliked; close to haram but not reaching the level of definitively forbidden.
استقبال (istiqbal): Facing the qibla directly.
استدبار (istidbar): Turning one's back to the qibla.
تمرتاشي (al-Tamurtashi): A later Hanafi scholar (d. 1004 AH) known for his work on fiqh, whose opinion is cited here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Makruh tahrimi
B) Makruh tanzihi
C) Not makruh according to al-Tamurtashi
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla during elimination is strictly disliked; during istinja, there is an intra-Hanafi difference, with al-Tamurtashi's choice that it is not makruh.

Sitting Posture and Prohibition of Speech During Relieving Oneself
Ruling and proof for sitting posture and speech prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended sitting posture and the ruling on speech during relieving oneself, and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Sit leaning on the left leg and do not speak—Allah detests unnecessary speech at the toilet.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text outlines the recommended etiquette for relieving oneself, focusing on the sitting posture and the prohibition of speech. We will examine the hadith provided as proof and understand the legal classification (makruh) based on the intensity of divine detestation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the two acts: sitting posture (recommended) and speech (prohibited unless necessary). Determine the hukm level for each from the text.
The text uses 'yajlis' (he sits) in the imperative form, indicating sunnah, and 'la yatakallam' (he does not speak) indicating prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim. Identify the key phrase: 'Allah detests that'.
The word 'yamqutu' (detests) is crucial for determining the level of prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The prohibition of talking while exposing private parts indicates detestation; here, the speech itself is linked to that context.
The hadith does not explicitly forbid speech alone, but the commentary applies it to any unnecessary talk.
4
Note the hukm level and ikhtilaf
The text concludes that speech is makruh (disliked) because 'maqt' means intense hatred. Some schools consider it haram, but Hanafi takes the milder view.
The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tahrimi (close to haram) due to the strong dislike.
5
Apply the ruling practically
The sitting posture: lean on left leg, right leg raised. Speech: only permissible for necessity (e.g., warning of danger). This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجلس مُعتمداً على يسَارِهِ، ولا يتكلّم، إلا لضرورة. والحشوش جمع الحش - بالفتح والضم- وهو بستان النخيل في الأصل، ثم استعمل في موضع قضاء الحاجة، لأنهم كانوا يقضون الحاجة فيها، والمحتضرة: الأمكنة التي يحضرها الشيطان، ويرصد فيها (1) بني آدم بالأذى والخبث - بضم الخاء والباء - جمع خبيث، وهو: المؤذي من الجن والإنس والشياطين، والخبائث جمع خبيثة، يريد ذكر ان الشياطين والجن وإناثهم. ويروى خبث -بسكون الباء- وهو مصدر بمعنى الشر، والاستعاذة منهم في البناء المعد لقضاء الحاجة، لأنه مأواهم، وفي الفضاء، لأنه يصير مأواهم بخروج الخارج. (ويجلس مُعتمداً على يسَارِهِ) مـن رجليه ناصباً اليمنى منهما، بأن يضع أصابعها على الأرض، ويرفع باقيها لأن ذلك أسهل لخروج الخارج ولأنه المناسب هنا، ويوسع فيما بين رجليه، ولا يتكلّم، إلا لضرورة) فإن الله يمقت على ذلك، قال : « لا يَخْرُجُ الرَّجُلانِ يَضْرِبَانِ الْغَائِطَ كَاشِفَيْنِ عَنْ عَوْرَتِهِمَا، يَتَحَدَّثَانِ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ يَمْقُتُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ ). رواه أبو داود والحاكم وصححه ومعنى يضربان الغائط: يأتيانه. قال أهل اللغة: يقال: ضربت الأرض، إذا أتيت الخلاء، وضربت في الأرض، إذا سافرت. والمقت: البغض. وقيل: أشده. والمقت وإن كان على المجموع، فبعض موجبات المقت مكروه
And he should sit leaning on his left (leg), and not speak except out of necessity. The word 'al-hushush' is the plural of 'hush' (with fatha and dammah), which originally means a palm garden, then was used for the place of relieving need because they used to relieve themselves therein. The word 'al-muhdara' refers to places frequented by Satan, where he lies in wait for humans with harm and evil (khabth, with damm on kha' and ba'), plural of khabith, meaning harmful beings from jinn, humans, and devils, and khaba'ith (plural of khabitha) refers to female devils and jinn. It is also recited as 'khabth' (with sukun on ba'), a verbal noun meaning evil. Seeking refuge from them is in a building prepared for relieving need, because it is their abode, and in open space, because it becomes their abode due to the exit of excrement. (And he should sit leaning on his left): from his legs, erecting the right one, placing its toes on the ground and raising the rest, because that is easier for the exit of excrement and more appropriate; and he should widen between his legs. And he should not speak except out of necessity, for Allah detests that. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Two men should not go out to defecate, both exposing their private parts, and then talk, for Allah detests that.' Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim, who authenticated it. The meaning of 'yadriban al-gha'it' is that they come to the toilet. The linguists say: 'daraba al-ard' means to come to the toilet, and 'daraba fi al-ard' means to travel. And 'al-maqt' means hatred, or the severest hatred. And although hatred is for the whole, some causes of hatred are disliked.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling and its proof for the etiquette of relieving oneself. The author begins by stating the ruling: one should sit leaning on the left leg, specifically raising the right foot with toes on the ground, and should not speak except for necessity. The commentary then explains a linguistic note on 'al-hushush' (latrines), which are places frequented by Satan, and the need to seek refuge. It then returns to the sitting posture details: the left leg is the base of support, right leg is raised for ease of excretion. The prohibition of speech is emphasized, and a hadith is cited: two men should not go out to relive themselves exposing their private parts and then talk, because Allah detests such behavior. The author explains key phrases: 'yadriban al-gha'it' means they come to the toilet; 'maqt' means intense hatred. The commentary concludes that the hatred pertains to the whole act, but some individual elements (like speech) are disliked (makruh). This aligns with the Hanafi principle that prohibition (tahrim) is established by strong proof, but here the hadith indicates detestation, not absolute prohibition.

Key Terms
يَمْقُتُ (yamqutu): Detests or hates intensely
الْمَقْتُ (al-maqt): Intense hatred or abhorrence

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because it disturbs others

Key Takeaway
The recommended sitting posture and the prohibition of speech during relieving oneself are based on a hadith indicating Allah's detestation, making the speech makruh (disliked) and not haram.

Prohibition of Facing the Qibla During Relieving
Ruling, proof, and intra-Hanafi dispute on facing qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla during relieving and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding purification (istinja).

Core Idea
Facing the qibla while relieving is makruh tahrimi, even in buildings.

This lesson examines the prohibition of facing or backing the qibla during relieving. We will explore the primary hadith evidence and discuss an intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether this prohibition extends to the subsequent purification (istinja).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
The base text states it is makruh tahrimi and cites the hadith 'When you go to the toilet, do not face the qibla...'. Identify the hadith and the level of ruling.
Makruh tahrimi is just below haram.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary mentions a difference: some scholars (including al-Tamartashi) do not consider facing during istinja as disliked. Identify the point of disagreement.
The disagreement is on the scope of the prohibition.
3
Examine the differing scholar's basis
Al-Tamartashi restricts the hadith to the act of elimination, not the subsequent cleansing. Understand his reasoning.
He likely uses qiyas or considers the hadith's context.
4
Analyze the response from the classical view
The text does not provide a strong rebuttal; it simply records the difference. Consider the weight of the general meaning of the hadith.
The classical view relies on the general application.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects whether one should avoid facing during istinja. Know the mufta bihi position.
The text suggests the classical view is safer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُكره تحريماً: استقبال القبلة، واستدبارها، ولو في البنيان . (ويُكْرَهُ تَحْرِيمَاً : اسْتِقْبَالُ القِبلَةِ بالفرج حال قضاء الحاجة. واختلفوا في الاستقبال للتطهير، واختار « التمرتاشي» أنه لا يكره (و) يكره ( اسْتِدْبَارُهَا ) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إذا أتَيْتُمُ الْغَائِطِ، فَلا تَسْتَقْبِلُوا الْقِبْلَةَ، وَلا تَسْتَدْبِرُوهَا، وَلَكِنْ شَرِّقُوا أَوْ غَرُبُوا . وهو بإطلاقه يتناول البناء والفضاء، فلذا قال: (وَلَو) في البُنْيَانِ) وإذا جلس مستقبلاً ناسياً، فتذكر، يستحب له الانحراف بقدر ما يمكنه. لما أخرجه الطبري مرفوعاً: «مَنْ جَلَسَ يُبولُ قبالة القبلة، فانْحَرَفَ عَنْهَا إجلالاً لهَا، لَمْ يقُمْ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ حَتَّى يُغْفَرُ لَهُ ).
And it is disliked with tahrimean: facing the qibla, and backing it, even if in a building. (And it is disliked with tahrimean: facing the qibla with the private part at the time of relieving need. And they differed regarding facing for purification, and al-Tamartashi chose that it is not disliked. And (he said) it is disliked to back it, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'When you come to the toilet, do not face the qibla nor back it; rather face east or west.' And its general meaning includes both building and open space, hence he said: 'even if in a building.' And if he sits facing it forgetfully and then remembers, it is recommended to turn away as much as he can, because of what al-Tabari narrated as marfu': 'Whoever sits to urinate facing the qibla and then turns away out of reverence for it, will not leave his seat until he is forgiven.'
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to face or back the qibla while relieving oneself, and this applies even inside a building. The commentary begins by specifying 'facing with the private part'. It then mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars considered facing the qibla during purification (istinja) also disliked, but al-Tamartashi chose that it is not disliked. The primary proof is the hadith commanding to face east or west, which generalizes to all places. The commentary then adds that if one forgetfully sits facing and then remembers, it is recommended to turn away, supported by another hadith promising forgiveness for such reverence. The Hanafi position holds that the prohibition is strong (makruh tahrimi) due to the explicit hadith, though some later scholars like al-Tamartashi restricted it.

Key Terms
تَحْرِيمَاً (tahriman): Prohibitively disliked; a level below haram but above makruh tanzih
الاسْتِقْبَال للتطهير (al-istiqbal li al-tathir): Facing the qibla during the purification process (istinja) after relieving

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for facing the qibla while cleansing oneself (istinja) according to al-Tamartashi?
A) Makruh tahrimi
B) Makruh tanzih
C) Not disliked (la yukrah)
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Facing or backing the qibla during relieving is makruh tahrimi; the disagreement on istinja demonstrates the richness of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Disliked Acts and Places When Relieving Oneself
List of makruh acts and places with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the disliked acts and places for relieving oneself according to the Hanafi school and explain the rationale and evidence for each.

Core Idea
Respecting Allah's creation and avoiding harm to others and oneself are the bases for these disliked acts.

This passage details various acts that are disliked (makruh) when answering the call of nature. The rulings stem from a balance between reverence for Allah's signs, consideration for other people, and protection from physical and spiritual harm. We will explore each prohibition and its supporting evidence, noting the difference between lightly disliked (makruh tanzih) and more strongly disliked (makruh tahrimi) acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Each act is introduced with 'يُكره' (it is disliked). Scan the Arabic to list them: facing sun/moon, wind direction, urinating/defecating in water, shade, hole, road, under fruit tree, standing, holding child to qibla, sitting low and urinating high, and urinating where one washes.
The term يكر (and ويُكره) signals dislike.
2
Note the rationale for each
For each act, a brief reason is given: sun/moon (reverence), wind (soiling), water (impurity), shade/road (hadith), hole (harm to creatures), fruit tree (destroys fruit), standing (splashing), child (disrespect), low-high (splashing), washing place (waswasa).
These rationales help remember the rulings.
3
Locate the dalil for the most serious acts
The hadith about the 'two cursed acts' (اللأَعِنَيْنِ) is quoted for the road and shade. The command 'اتَّقُوا' (beware) indicates a stronger prohibition, making these acts makruh tahrimi.
This is a Sunnah ahad hadith; its thubut is qati but dalala zanni.
4
Classify the level of dislike
Most acts are makruh tanzih (lightly disliked), but the road and shade are makruh tahrimi due to explicit prohibition. Standing is disliked unless excused.
The mufta bihi position is that road/shade are makruh tahrimi; others tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستقبال عين الشمس والقمر، ومهب الريح. ويُكره أن يبول، أوْ يَتَغَوَّطَ في الماء، والظل، والجخر، والطريق، وتحت شجرة مثمرة، والبولُ قائماً، إلا من عدر. ويكره إمساك الصبي نحو القبلة للبول (وَ) يكر (استقبال عين الشمس، والقمر) احتراماً لهما، لأنهما آيتان عظيمتان من آيات الله الباهرة ( ومهب الريح)؛ لأنه يعود عليه بالخارج منه فينجسه، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها، ويُكره أن يبول، أوْ يَتَغَوَّطَ في المَاءِ) ولو كان جارياً، وكذا بقرب ماء كثير، ونهر وعين وحوض (والظل) الذي ينفتع بالجلوس فيه، (والجخر)) سواء كان جحر فأرة أو حية أو نملة، أو غيرها، لحصول الأذى منه )، أو لَهُ. (والطَّرِيقِ) والمقبرة، للنهي عنه بقوله : ( اتَّقُوا اللأَعِنَيْنِ، قَالُوا: وَمَا اللاعِنَانِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ الَّذِي يَتَخَلَّى فِي طَرِيقِ النَّاسِ أَوْ ظِلِّهِمْ . وَتَحْتَ شَجَرَةٍ مُنْمِرَةٍ؛ لإتلاف الثمر وتنجيسه. (و) يكره (البَوْلُ قَائِمَاً)؛ لأنه يصيبه منه غالباً إلا من عُدْرٍ ، كوجع بصلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع، ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه، لأنه يورث الوسوسة.
And (it is disliked) facing the sun and moon, and the direction of the wind. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, shade, hole, road, under a fruit-bearing tree, and standing urination except due to an excuse. And it is disliked to hold a child facing the qibla for urination. (And it is disliked) facing the sun and moon out of respect for them, because they are two great signs of Allah. (And the direction of the wind) because the excrement may blow back on him and soil him. And it is disliked to sit in a low place and urinate in a higher place. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, even if flowing, and similarly near a large body of water, river, spring, or basin. (And shade) that is beneficial for sitting. (And the hole) whether a mouse hole, snake hole, ant hole, or other, because harm may come from it or to it. (And the road and cemetery) due to the prohibition in his statement: 'Beware of the two cursed acts.' They said: 'What are the two cursed acts, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'The one who relieves himself in the people's path or their shade.' (And under a fruit-bearing tree) because it destroys the fruit and makes it impure. (And) it is disliked (standing urination) because it often splashes on him, except due to an excuse like pain in his back. And it is disliked to urinate in a place and then perform wudu or bathe there, because it causes waswasa (anxiety).
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage enumerates multiple disliked (makruh) acts and places during relieving oneself. The author lists: facing the sun or moon (out of respect for Allah's signs), facing the wind direction (due to risk of soiling), urinating/defecating in water (even flowing), in shade, in a hole, in a road (supported by the hadith about 'two cursed acts'), under a fruit-bearing tree, standing up (except for excuse), and urinating in a place where one washes (causes waswasa). For each, a brief rationale is given: for sun and moon, reverence; for wind, potential soiling; for water, the water may become impure; for shade, it disturbs others; for hole, harm to creatures; for road, causing curse; for tree, damage to fruit; for standing, risk of splashing; for washing place, anxiety. The hadith about 'لاعنين' (two cursed acts) provides strong evidence against relieving in public paths and shade. The Hanafi school considers these acts makruh tahrimi or tanzih depending on the context; the text seems to consider them dislike with religious disapproval.

Key Terms
اللأَعِنَيْنِ (al-la'inayn): Two acts that invite curse (from people or angels); specifically relieving in the path or shade.
الوَسْوَسَة (al-waswasa): Anxiety or whispering (from Satan) about purity; caused by urinating in a place where one later performs wudu.
الجخر (al-jukhur (or al-jahur?)): Hole or burrow where animals dwell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is urinating under a fruit-bearing tree disliked according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it harms the tree
B) Because it destroys the fruit and makes it impure
C) Because it attracts animals
D) Because it wastes water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits using public pathways and shade for relieving as makruh tahrimi, while lightly discouraging other acts for respect and hygiene.

Recommended Acts When Entering the Toilet
List of recommended and disliked actions for entering the toilet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) and disliked (makruh) actions when entering the toilet according to the Hanafi school, and explain the rationale behind each.

Core Idea
The toilet is a place of impurity; thus, actions that honor Allah's name or the prayer garment are prohibited, while silence and discretion are recommended.

In this lesson, we explore the etiquettes (adab) of entering the toilet as outlined in Imdad al-Fattah. The Hanafi school prescribes a set of recommended behaviors to maintain purity and reverence, and prohibits actions that could lead to disrespect or distraction. Understanding these rulings helps the believer maintain proper decorum in all states.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between mustahabb and makruh
Identify which actions in the text are recommended (mustahabb) and which are disliked (makruh). Understand that recommended actions earn reward, while disliked actions are discouraged but not sinful.
The text uses 'yastahibbu' for recommended and 'yukrahu' for disliked.
2
Understand the garment recommendation
Why is it recommended to wear a different garment? To protect the prayer garment from impurity. If you cannot change, be cautious. This shows the importance of keeping the prayer garment pure.
The phrase 'إن كان له ذلك' indicates a conditional recommendation.
3
Analyze the prohibition of mentioning Allah
The text lists several prohibitions: not praising Allah after sneezing, not responding to sneeze or greeting, not answering adhan. The common reason: the toilet is not a place for dhikr. Even though these acts are normally virtuous, they are suspended here to avoid disrespect.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; some schools allow silent dhikr.
4
List other prohibited actions and their common theme
Actions like spitting, blowing nose, clearing throat, turning around, and fidgeting are all prohibited. They either produce impurity or cause distraction. The goal is to focus on the act of relieving oneself with minimal disturbance.
These are all considered makruh tanzih.
5
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Consider a person wearing a ring with the name 'Allah'. The ruling is to remove it before entering. Likewise, if one has a phone with a Quran app, it should be closed or left outside to avoid carrying sacred text into the toilet.
The illa (reason) is the presence of Allah's name or Quranic verses in an impure place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب له دخول الخلاء بثوب غير الذي يصلي فيه، إن كان له ذلك، وإلا فيحترز، ويحفظ ثوبه عن النجاسة، والماء المستعمل، ويكره دخوله ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى، أو شيء من القرآن) ، ولا يكشف عورته قائماً)، ولا يذكر الله، فلا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد سلاماً، ولا يجيب مؤذناً، ولا ينظر لعورته، ولا إلى ما يخرج منه، ولا يبصق، ولا يمتخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفاف، ولا يعبث ببدنه،
And it is recommended for him to enter the toilet with a garment other than the one in which he prays, if he has that; otherwise, he should be cautious and protect his garment from impurity and used water. And it is disliked to enter with a ring on which is written Allah's name or something from the Quran. And he should not uncover his private part while standing. And he should not mention Allah, so if he sneezes, he should not praise Allah; he should not respond to a sneezer; he should not return a greeting; he should not answer the mu'adhdhin; he should not look at his private part nor at what exits from him; he should not spit; he should not blow his nose; he should not clear his throat; he should not turn around excessively; and he should not fidget with his body.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage details recommended (mustahabb) and disliked (makruh) actions for one entering the toilet. It is recommended to wear a garment different from the one used for prayer to avoid bringing impurity into the prayer garment. If that is not possible, one should be careful to protect the garment. It is disliked to enter with a ring bearing Allah's name or Quranic verses. Several actions are prohibited: raising the garment while standing (rather, one should wait until near the ground), mentioning Allah's name (including praising after a sneeze), responding to greetings or the adhan, looking at the private parts or exit, spitting, blowing nose, clearing throat, excessive turning, and fidgeting. These etiquettes maintain the sanctity of the act and prevent distraction. The proofs for these are found in authentic hadiths (some cited in the commentary). The Hanafi school considers these as adab (etiquettes), not obligatory, but strongly recommended.

Key Terms
الوَسْوَسَة (al-waswasa): Whisperings of Satan causing anxiety about purity
التَّمَحْنُحُ (al-tamahnuh): Clearing the throat audibly

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it recommended to wear a different garment when entering the toilet?
A) Because the prayer garment may become impure
B) Because it is more comfortable
C) Because it is a sunnah
D) Because it separates between prayer and toilet use

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes specific etiquettes for the toilet to maintain reverence for Allah's name and purity of the prayer garment.
