Makruhat of Place and Posture When Relieving Oneself
Exposition of disliked locations and postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the disliked locations (water, shade, hole, road, under fruit tree, facing sun/moon/wind) and the disliked posture of urinating standing, with their proofs.

Core Idea
Certain places and postures are makruh because they cause harm, disrespect Allah's signs, or originate from prophetic prohibition.

In this passage, the author details various actions that are disliked (makruh) when relieving oneself. These include specific locations where one should not relieve himself, such as in water, on roads, or under fruit trees, as well as postures like urinating while standing. The rulings are based on prophetic hadith and the principle of avoiding harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Read the text and list each action mentioned as disliked, e.g., urinating/defecating in water, in shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit tree, facing the sun or moon, facing the wind, urinating standing.
Some acts have explicit hadith evidence, others are based on reasoning.
2
Determine the ruling level
The text uses 'yukrah' (it is disliked). In Hanafi fiqh, this is primarily makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), but some acts like relieving on roads/shade may be makruh tahrimi due to severe warning.
3
Locate the evidence
For the road and shade, the hadith of the two curses is cited. For the hole, a hadith prohibiting urinating in a hole is mentioned. For others, the reasoning is given: harm to creatures, disrespect to Allah's signs, etc.
4
Understand the wisdom
Reflect on why each act is disliked: e.g., urinating in water contaminates it, urinating in shade deprives others of beneficial shade, urinating in a hole may harm animals or the person, etc.
5
Note exceptions
The text explicitly allows urinating standing if one has an excuse like back pain. This shows that some rulings have flexibility based on necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستقبال عين الشمس والقمر ، ومهب الريح. ويُكره أن يبول، أوْ يَتَغَوَّطَ في الماء، والظل، والجخر، والطريق، وتحت شجرة مثمرة، والبولُ قائماً، إلا من عدرٍ.
ويكره إمساك الصبي نحو القبلة للبول (وَ) يكر (استقبال عين الشمس، والقمر) احتراماً لهما، لأنهما آيتان عظيمتان من آيات الله الباهرة ( ومهب الريح)؛ لأنه يعود عليه بالخارج منه فينجسه، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها، ويُكره أن يبول، أوْ يَتَغَوَّطَ في المَاءِ) ولو كان جارياً، وكذا بقرب ماء كثير، ونهر وعين وحوض (والظل) الذي ينفتع بالجلوس فيه، (والجخر)) سواء كان جحر فأرة أو حية أو نملة، أو غيرها، لحصول الأذى منه )، أو لَهُ. (والطَّرِيقِ) والمقبرة، للنهي عنه بقوله : ( اتَّقُوا اللأَعِنَيْنِ، قَالُوا: وَمَا اللاعِنَانِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ الَّذِي يَتَخَلَّى فِي طَرِيقِ النَّاسِ أَوْ ظِلْهِمْ . وَتَحْتَ شَجَرَةٍ مُنْمِرَةٍ؛ لإتلاف الثمر وتنجيسه. (و) يكره (البَوْلُ قَائِمَاً)؛ لأنه يصيبه منه غالباً إلا من عُدْرٍ ، كوجع بصلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع، ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه، لأنه يورث الوسوسة. ويستحب له دخول الخلاء بثوب غير الذي يصلي فيه، إن كان له ذلك، وإلا فيحترز، ويحفظ ثوبه عن النجاسة، والماء المستعمل، ويكره دخوله ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى، أو شيء من القرآن) ، ولا يكشف عورته قائماً)، ولا يذكر الله، فلا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد سلاماً، ولا يجيب مؤذناً، ولا ينظر لعورته، ولا إلى ما يخرج منه، ولا يبصق، ولا يمتخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفاف، ولا يعبث ببدنه،
(۱) لقوله : « لا يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي جُحْرٍ»، أخرجه النسائي في الطهارة، باب كراهيـة البـول في الجحر (٣٤). والجحر الخرق في الأرض والجدار. ط.
(۲) فقد نقل أن سعد ابن عبادة الخزرجي بال في جحر بأرض حوران فقتله الجن. انظر الطبقات الكبرى (٦١٧/٣). (۳) أخرجه مسلم في الطهارة، باب النهي عن التخلي في الطريق والظلال (٢٦۹) ، وأبو داود في الطهارة، باب: المواضع التي نهى النبي عن البول فيها (٢٥). (٤) لقوله : « لا يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي مُسْتَحَمِّهِ ثُمَّ يَغْتَسِلُ فِيهِ أو يَتَوَضَّأُ فَإِنَّ عَامَّةَ الْوَسْوَاسِ مِنْهُ»، أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب: البول في المستحم (۲۷)، والنسائي في الطهارة، باب كراهية البول في المستحم (٣٦). (٥) لما روي عن أنس قال: «كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا دَخَلَ الْخَلاءَ نَزَعَ خَاتَمَهُ، أي: لأن نقشه محمد رسول الله. أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب الخاتم يكون فيه ذكر الله تعالى (۱۹).
(٦) لقول أنس : « كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ إِذَا أَرَادَ الْحَاجَةَ لَمْ يَرْفَعُ ثَوْبَهُ حَتَّى يَدْنُو مِنْ الأرض»، أخرجه الترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في الاستتار عند الحاجة (١٤).
ويخرُجُ مِنَ الخَلاءِ برجله اليمنى، ثُمَّ يقولُ: الحمدُ لله الذي أَذْهَبَ عني الأذى، وعافاني.
(۲)
ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء، ولا يطيل الجلوس، فإنه يورث الباسور (") ووجــع الكبد. (ويخـرج مـن الخلاء برجلِهِ اليُمْنَى)؛ لأنها نقلت من المكروه ومحل الشياطين، فكان نعمة، واليمين أولى بها. (ثُمَّ يقولُ) بعد الخروج: (الحَمْدُ للهِ الَّذي أَذهَبَ عني الأذى بإخراج الفضلات الرديئة التي لو حبست في الجسد أمرضته. (وَعَافَانِي) بإبقاء خاصية الغذاء، لأنه لو خرج جميعـــه كــان مـهلكاً. وروي عــن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « غُفْرَانَكَ » (۳). وذكروا له وجهين: أحدهما، كان عليه الصلاة والسلام رأى تــرك ذكر الله تعالى زمان لبثه في الخلاء، تقصيراً منه، فتداركه بالاستغفار فإنه كان يذكر الله تعالى عـلـى سائر أحواله. والثاني: أن الاستغفار هنا كناية عن الاعتراف بالقصور عن بلوغ حق شكر نعمـة الإطعام، وتربية الغذاء من حين التناول إلى أوان الانهضام وتسهيل خروج الأذى، بسلامة البدن مــن الآلام، فالتجأ إلى الاستغفار، اعترافاً بالقصور عن شكر الإنعام.
(۱) قوله: (ولا يذكر الله إلخ) بل يكره مطلق الكلام حال قضاء الحاجة والمجامعة إلا لحاجة تفوت بالتأخير كتحذير نحو أعمى من سقوط. قوله: (فلا يحمد إذا عطس إلخ) وله أن يفعل ذلك في نفسه من غير تلفظ بلسانه. قوله: (ولا ينظر لعورته) فإنه خلاف الأدب وكذا الأولى عدم نظر أحد الزوجين إلى عورة الآخر، وكما يندب لـه الستر يندب تغطية رأسه وخفض صوته. قال علي له من أكثر النظر إلى سوءته عوقب بالنسيان اهــــ وقيل: من أكثر مسها ابتلي بالزنا. قوله: (ولا إلى الخارج) فإنه يورث النسيان وهو مستقذر شرعاً ولا داعيـة لـه. قوله: ( ولا يبصق لأنه يصفر الأسنان، قوله: (ولا يتمخط) لامتلاء أنفه بالرائحة الكريهة، قوله: (ولا يكثر الالتفاف إلخ لأن محل حضور الشياطين فلا يفعل فيه ما لا حاجة إليه قوله: (ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء) لأنه محل التفكر في آياتها وليس هذا محله قوله: (فإنه يورث الباسور ووجع الكبد) روي ذلك عن لقمان الحكيم، ولأنه محل الشياطين، فيستحب الإسراع بالخروج منه. ط. (۲) الباسور: طية سميكة من الغشاء المخاطي في أسفل شق شرجي. ج ( بواسير). وتطلق البواسير عامة على مرض
يحدث تمدد وريدي دوالي في الشرج على الأشهر تحت الغشاء المخاطي. المعجم الوسيط / بسر /. (۳) أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب ما يقول الرجل إذا خرج من الخلاء (۳۰)، والترمذي في الطهارة، باب: مـا يقول إذا خرج من الخلاء (۷).
And facing the sun and moon, and the direction of the wind. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, in shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit-bearing tree, and urinating standing, except due to an excuse.
And it is disliked to hold a child towards the qibla for urination. (And) it is disliked (facing the sun and moon) out of respect for them, because they are two great signs of Allah's manifest signs, (and the direction of the wind) because the impurity may blow back on him and soil him. And it is disliked to sit at the bottom of a slope and urinate at the top. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, even if it is flowing, and similarly near a large quantity of water, a river, a spring, or a basin. (And) (in shade) that is beneficial to sit in, (and in a hole) whether it is a mouse hole, a snake hole, an ant hole, or others, because of the harm caused to it or from it. (And on a road) and a cemetery, due to the prohibition in his statement: 'Beware of the two curses.' They said: 'What are the two curses, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'The one who relieves himself on the people's path or in their shade.' And under a fruit-bearing tree, because it destroys the fruit and soils it. (And) it is disliked (urinating standing) because it often splashes on him, except due to an excuse, such as a pain in his lower back. And it is disliked to urinate in a place where he then performs wudu or ghusl, because it causes waswasa (whisperings). And it is recommended for him to enter the lavatory with a garment other than the one he prays in, if he has that; otherwise, he should be cautious and protect his garment from impurity and used water. And it is disliked to enter with a ring on which is written Allah's name or something from the Quran. And he should not uncover his private part while standing. And he should not remember Allah, so he should not say 'Alhamdulillah' if he sneezes, nor respond to a sneezer, nor return a greeting, nor answer the call to prayer. And he should not look at his private part, nor at what comes out of him. And he should not spit, nor blow his nose, nor clear his throat. And he should not turn around excessively, nor play with his body.
(1) Because of his statement: 'Let none of you urinate in a hole.' Narrated by al-Nasa'i in Taharah, chapter on dislike of urinating in a hole (34). And a hole is an opening in the ground or wall. (2) It is reported that Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah al-Khazraji urinated in a hole in the land of Hawran and the jinn killed him. See al-Tabaqat al-Kubra (3/617). (3) Narrated by Muslim in Taharah, chapter on the prohibition of relieving oneself on the road and in the shade (269), and Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter: Places which the Prophet forbade urinating in (25). (4) Because of his statement: 'Let none of you urinate in his bathing place then perform ghusl or wudu in it, for most waswasa comes from that.' Narrated by Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter: Urinating in the bathing place (27), and al-Nasa'i in Taharah, chapter on dislike of urinating in the bathing place (36). (5) Because it is related from Anas that he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah entered the lavatory, he removed his ring, i.e., because its engraving was Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah.' Narrated by Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter on the ring containing Allah's name (19). (6) Because of the statement of Anas: 'When the Messenger of Allah wanted to relieve himself, he did not lift his garment until he came close to the ground.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter on covering oneself when relieving oneself (14).
And he exits from the lavatory with his right foot, then says: Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm and gave me well-being.
(2)
And he should not raise his eyes to the sky, nor prolong sitting, for that causes hemorrhoids and liver pain. (And he exits from the lavatory with his right foot) because it is removed from the disliked and the place of devils, so it is a blessing, and the right is more deserving of it. (Then he says) after exiting: (Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm by expelling the vile wastes which, if retained in the body, would make it ill. (And He gave me well-being) by preserving the essence of nutrition, because if it all exited, it would be destructive. And it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'Your forgiveness.' And they mentioned two interpretations: One is that he (peace be upon him) saw the abandonment of remembering Allah during his stay in the lavatory as a shortcoming from him, so he made up for it with Istighfar, for he used to remember Allah in all his states. The second is that Istighfar here is a metaphor for acknowledging the inability to fulfil the due of giving thanks for the blessing of feeding and nurturing the food from the time of consumption to the time of digestion and facilitating the exit of harm, with the safety of the body from pains, so he resorted to Istighfar, admitting the shortcoming of gratitude for the blessings.
(1) His statement: (And he should not remember Allah, etc.) Rather, it is disliked to speak absolutely while relieving oneself and during intercourse, except for a need that would be lost if delayed, such as warning a blind person about falling. His statement: (So he should not say 'Alhamdulillah' if he sneezes, etc.) He may do that in his heart without uttering it with his tongue. His statement: (And he should not look at his private part) For that is contrary to good manners, and similarly it is better for spouses not to look at each other's private parts. And just as covering is recommended for him, so is covering his head and lowering his voice. 'Ali said: Whoever looks excessively at his private part is punished with forgetfulness. And it is said: Whoever touches it excessively is afflicted with adultery. His statement: (Nor at what comes out) For it causes forgetfulness and is legally filthy, and there is no need for it. His statement: (Nor should he spit) because it yellows the teeth. His statement: (Nor should he blow his nose) due to filling his nose with a bad smell. His statement: (Nor should he turn around excessively, etc.) Because it is a place where devils are present, so one should not do anything unnecessary there. His statement: (Nor should he raise his eyes to the sky) because it is a place for reflecting on its signs, and this is not its place. His statement: (For it causes hemorrhoids and liver pain) That is related from Luqman the Wise, and because it is a place of devils, so it is recommended to hasten exiting from it. (2) Hemorrhoid: a thick fold of mucous membrane at the bottom of the anal fissure. Plural (hemorrhoids). And hemorrhoids are generally called a disease that causes varicose veins in the anus, commonly under the mucous membrane. Al-Mu'jam al-Wasit / bsr /. (3) Narrated by Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter on what a man says when he exits the lavatory (30), and al-Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter: What he says when he exits the lavatory (7).
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (Sharh) on Nur al-Idah, explaining the disliked and recommended actions when relieving oneself. The author begins by listing several makruhat (disliked actions): facing the sun or moon directly, because they are great signs of Allah and deserve respect; facing the direction of the wind, because the impurity may blow back; urinating or defecating in water, even flowing water, and similarly near a large body of water; in a shade that people use; in a hole (any animal hole) due to possible harm to the creature or oneself; on a road or in a cemetery, citing the hadith of the 'two curses'—the one who relieves himself in people's path or their shade; under a fruit-bearing tree because the fruit becomes impure; and urinating while standing, unless one has an excuse like back pain. The author then mentions it is disliked to urinate in a place where one later performs wudu or ghusl, as it causes waswasa (obsessive whispers). Then the recommendable (mustahabb) acts: entering the lavatory with a different garment from the salah garment, and protecting one's clothes from impurity and used water. It is disliked to enter with a ring containing Allah's name or Quranic verses. One should not uncover his private part while standing. One should not engage in dhikr (remembrance of Allah), so one does not praise Allah for sneezing, thank a sneezer, return greetings, or respond to the adhan while relieving oneself. One should not look at one's private part or at the excrement. One should not spit, blow nose, clear throat, turn excessively, or fidget. When exiting, one should step out with the right foot, praising Allah for removing harm and granting well-being (the du'a 'Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba 'anni al-adha wa 'afani). The author also mentions the Prophet's du'a 'Ghufranak' (Your forgiveness) and provides two interpretations: first, that the Prophet felt he had fallen short in dhikr during his stay and sought forgiveness, and second, that it is an admission of the inability to fully thank Allah for the blessings of digestion and expulsion. The commentary also includes additional notes from super-commentary, such as the permissibility of speaking when necessary (like warning a blind person) and the recommendation to cover the head and lower voice.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khalā'): The lavatory or place for relieving oneself.
البول قائماً (al-bawl qā'iman): Urinating while standing. It is disliked except for an excuse.
الجحر (al-juḥr): A hole in the ground or wall, especially those of animals.
الوسوسة (al-waswasah): Whisperings or obsessive thoughts from Shaytan, especially related to purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the text, which two acts are called 'the two curses' (اللاعنان)?
A) Urinating in water and on roads.
B) Relieving oneself on people's path or in their shade.
C) Facing the sun and moon while relieving.
D) Urinating in a hole and under a tree.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that relieving oneself in certain places and postures is disliked based on prophetic guidance and the principle of avoiding harm.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
Mustahabbat and Etiquettes of Entering and Exiting the Lavatory
Exposition of recommended and prohibited conduct in the lavatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended actions when entering and exiting the lavatory, the prohibited conduct (like speaking, looking), and the proper supplications.

Core Idea
Entering the lavatory with the right foot and exiting with the right, concealing oneself, and avoiding Allah's remembrance are all part of prophetic adab.

The passage now turns to the mustahabbat (recommended) actions and additional guidelines for conduct in the lavatory. These include entering with a different garment, removing rings with Allah's name, not speaking, not looking at private parts, and the well-known supplications upon entering and exiting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mustahabbat
The text lists recommended acts: entering with a different garment, exiting with the right foot, saying the du'a upon exiting, and not prolonging sitting. Also, the sunnah of removing the ring with Allah's name.
2
Understand the prohibited acts
The text also lists makruh acts in this context: entering with a ring with Allah's name, uncovering the private part while standing, speaking, looking at private parts, spitting, etc.
3
Learn the supplications
The du'a for exiting is 'Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba anni al-adha wa afani'. The Prophet also said 'Ghufranak' which is interpreted as seeking forgiveness for the inability to thank Allah properly.
4
Reflect on the wisdom
Most of these etiquettes are about modesty, hygiene, and reverence for Allah. For example, not mentioning Allah's name in the lavatory is out of respect.
5
Apply the adab
In practice, one should enter with the left foot, remove any item bearing Allah's name, avoid speech, and exit with the right foot reciting the supplication.
The left foot is used for entering places of contamination, right for exiting.

واستقبال عين الشمس والقمر ، ومهب الريح. ويُكره أن يبول، أوْ يَتَغَوَّطَ في الماء، والظل، والجخر، والطريق، وتحت شجرة مثمرة، والبولُ قائماً، إلا من عدرٍ.
ويكره إمساك الصبي نحو القبلة للبول (وَ) يكر (استقبال عين الشمس، والقمر) احتراماً لهما، لأنهما آيتان عظيمتان من آيات الله الباهرة ( ومهب الريح)؛ لأنه يعود عليه بالخارج منه فينجسه، ويكره أن يقعد في أسفل الأرض ويبول في أعلاها، ويُكره أن يبول، أوْ يَتَغَوَّطَ في المَاءِ) ولو كان جارياً، وكذا بقرب ماء كثير، ونهر وعين وحوض (والظل) الذي ينفتع بالجلوس فيه، (والجخر)) سواء كان جحر فأرة أو حية أو نملة، أو غيرها، لحصول الأذى منه )، أو لَهُ. (والطَّرِيقِ) والمقبرة، للنهي عنه بقوله : ( اتَّقُوا اللأَعِنَيْنِ، قَالُوا: وَمَا اللاعِنَانِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ الَّذِي يَتَخَلَّى فِي طَرِيقِ النَّاسِ أَوْ ظِلْهِمْ . وَتَحْتَ شَجَرَةٍ مُنْمِرَةٍ؛ لإتلاف الثمر وتنجيسه. (و) يكره (البَوْلُ قَائِمَاً)؛ لأنه يصيبه منه غالباً إلا من عُدْرٍ ، كوجع بصلبه، ويكره أن يبول في موضع، ويتوضأ أو يغتسل فيه، لأنه يورث الوسوسة. ويستحب له دخول الخلاء بثوب غير الذي يصلي فيه، إن كان له ذلك، وإلا فيحترز، ويحفظ ثوبه عن النجاسة، والماء المستعمل، ويكره دخوله ومعه خاتم مكتوب عليه اسم الله تعالى، أو شيء من القرآن) ، ولا يكشف عورته قائماً)، ولا يذكر الله، فلا يحمد إذا عطس، ولا يشمت عاطساً، ولا يرد سلاماً، ولا يجيب مؤذناً، ولا ينظر لعورته، ولا إلى ما يخرج منه، ولا يبصق، ولا يمتخط، ولا يتنحنح، ولا يكثر الالتفاف، ولا يعبث ببدنه،
(۱) لقوله : « لا يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي جُحْرٍ»، أخرجه النسائي في الطهارة، باب كراهيـة البـول في الجحر (٣٤). والجحر الخرق في الأرض والجدار. ط.
(۲) فقد نقل أن سعد ابن عبادة الخزرجي بال في جحر بأرض حوران فقتله الجن. انظر الطبقات الكبرى (٦١٧/٣). (۳) أخرجه مسلم في الطهارة، باب النهي عن التخلي في الطريق والظلال (٢٦۹) ، وأبو داود في الطهارة، باب: المواضع التي نهى النبي عن البول فيها (٢٥). (٤) لقوله : « لا يَبُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي مُسْتَحَمِّهِ ثُمَّ يَغْتَسِلُ فِيهِ أو يَتَوَضَّأُ فَإِنَّ عَامَّةَ الْوَسْوَاسِ مِنْهُ»، أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب: البول في المستحم (۲۷)، والنسائي في الطهارة، باب كراهية البول في المستحم (٣٦). (٥) لما روي عن أنس قال: «كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا دَخَلَ الْخَلاءَ نَزَعَ خَاتَمَهُ، أي: لأن نقشه محمد رسول الله. أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب الخاتم يكون فيه ذكر الله تعالى (۱۹).
(٦) لقول أنس : « كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ إِذَا أَرَادَ الْحَاجَةَ لَمْ يَرْفَعُ ثَوْبَهُ حَتَّى يَدْنُو مِنْ الأرض»، أخرجه الترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في الاستتار عند الحاجة (١٤).
ويخرُجُ مِنَ الخَلاءِ برجله اليمنى، ثُمَّ يقولُ: الحمدُ لله الذي أَذْهَبَ عني الأذى، وعافاني.
(۲)
ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء، ولا يطيل الجلوس، فإنه يورث الباسور (") ووجــع الكبد. (ويخـرج مـن الخلاء برجلِهِ اليُمْنَى)؛ لأنها نقلت من المكروه ومحل الشياطين، فكان نعمة، واليمين أولى بها. (ثُمَّ يقولُ) بعد الخروج: (الحَمْدُ للهِ الَّذي أَذهَبَ عني الأذى بإخراج الفضلات الرديئة التي لو حبست في الجسد أمرضته. (وَعَافَانِي) بإبقاء خاصية الغذاء، لأنه لو خرج جميعـــه كــان مـهلكاً. وروي عــن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « غُفْرَانَكَ » (۳). وذكروا له وجهين: أحدهما، كان عليه الصلاة والسلام رأى تــرك ذكر الله تعالى زمان لبثه في الخلاء، تقصيراً منه، فتداركه بالاستغفار فإنه كان يذكر الله تعالى عـلـى سائر أحواله. والثاني: أن الاستغفار هنا كناية عن الاعتراف بالقصور عن بلوغ حق شكر نعمـة الإطعام، وتربية الغذاء من حين التناول إلى أوان الانهضام وتسهيل خروج الأذى، بسلامة البدن مــن الآلام، فالتجأ إلى الاستغفار، اعترافاً بالقصور عن شكر الإنعام.
(۱) قوله: (ولا يذكر الله إلخ) بل يكره مطلق الكلام حال قضاء الحاجة والمجامعة إلا لحاجة تفوت بالتأخير كتحذير نحو أعمى من سقوط. قوله: (فلا يحمد إذا عطس إلخ) وله أن يفعل ذلك في نفسه من غير تلفظ بلسانه. قوله: (ولا ينظر لعورته) فإنه خلاف الأدب وكذا الأولى عدم نظر أحد الزوجين إلى عورة الآخر، وكما يندب لـه الستر يندب تغطية رأسه وخفض صوته. قال علي له من أكثر النظر إلى سوءته عوقب بالنسيان اهــــ وقيل: من أكثر مسها ابتلي بالزنا. قوله: (ولا إلى الخارج) فإنه يورث النسيان وهو مستقذر شرعاً ولا داعيـة لـه. قوله: ( ولا يبصق لأنه يصفر الأسنان، قوله: (ولا يتمخط) لامتلاء أنفه بالرائحة الكريهة، قوله: (ولا يكثر الالتفاف إلخ لأن محل حضور الشياطين فلا يفعل فيه ما لا حاجة إليه قوله: (ولا يرفع بصره إلى السماء) لأنه محل التفكر في آياتها وليس هذا محله قوله: (فإنه يورث الباسور ووجع الكبد) روي ذلك عن لقمان الحكيم، ولأنه محل الشياطين، فيستحب الإسراع بالخروج منه. ط. (۲) الباسور: طية سميكة من الغشاء المخاطي في أسفل شق شرجي. ج ( بواسير). وتطلق البواسير عامة على مرض
يحدث تمدد وريدي دوالي في الشرج على الأشهر تحت الغشاء المخاطي. المعجم الوسيط / بسر /. (۳) أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب ما يقول الرجل إذا خرج من الخلاء (۳۰)، والترمذي في الطهارة، باب: مـا يقول إذا خرج من الخلاء (۷).
And facing the sun and moon, and the direction of the wind. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, in shade, in a hole, on a road, under a fruit-bearing tree, and urinating standing, except due to an excuse.
And it is disliked to hold a child towards the qibla for urination. (And) it is disliked (facing the sun and moon) out of respect for them, because they are two great signs of Allah's manifest signs, (and the direction of the wind) because the impurity may blow back on him and soil him. And it is disliked to sit at the bottom of a slope and urinate at the top. And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, even if it is flowing, and similarly near a large quantity of water, a river, a spring, or a basin. (And) (in shade) that is beneficial to sit in, (and in a hole) whether it is a mouse hole, a snake hole, an ant hole, or others, because of the harm caused to it or from it. (And on a road) and a cemetery, due to the prohibition in his statement: 'Beware of the two curses.' They said: 'What are the two curses, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'The one who relieves himself on the people's path or in their shade.' And under a fruit-bearing tree, because it destroys the fruit and soils it. (And) it is disliked (urinating standing) because it often splashes on him, except due to an excuse, such as a pain in his lower back. And it is disliked to urinate in a place where he then performs wudu or ghusl, because it causes waswasa (whisperings). And it is recommended for him to enter the lavatory with a garment other than the one he prays in, if he has that; otherwise, he should be cautious and protect his garment from impurity and used water. And it is disliked to enter with a ring on which is written Allah's name or something from the Quran. And he should not uncover his private part while standing. And he should not remember Allah, so he should not say 'Alhamdulillah' if he sneezes, nor respond to a sneezer, nor return a greeting, nor answer the call to prayer. And he should not look at his private part, nor at what comes out of him. And he should not spit, nor blow his nose, nor clear his throat. And he should not turn around excessively, nor play with his body.
(1) Because of his statement: 'Let none of you urinate in a hole.' Narrated by al-Nasa'i in Taharah, chapter on dislike of urinating in a hole (34). And a hole is an opening in the ground or wall. (2) It is reported that Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah al-Khazraji urinated in a hole in the land of Hawran and the jinn killed him. See al-Tabaqat al-Kubra (3/617). (3) Narrated by Muslim in Taharah, chapter on the prohibition of relieving oneself on the road and in the shade (269), and Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter: Places which the Prophet forbade urinating in (25). (4) Because of his statement: 'Let none of you urinate in his bathing place then perform ghusl or wudu in it, for most waswasa comes from that.' Narrated by Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter: Urinating in the bathing place (27), and al-Nasa'i in Taharah, chapter on dislike of urinating in the bathing place (36). (5) Because it is related from Anas that he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah entered the lavatory, he removed his ring, i.e., because its engraving was Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah.' Narrated by Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter on the ring containing Allah's name (19). (6) Because of the statement of Anas: 'When the Messenger of Allah wanted to relieve himself, he did not lift his garment until he came close to the ground.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter on covering oneself when relieving oneself (14).
And he exits from the lavatory with his right foot, then says: Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm and gave me well-being.
(2)
And he should not raise his eyes to the sky, nor prolong sitting, for that causes hemorrhoids and liver pain. (And he exits from the lavatory with his right foot) because it is removed from the disliked and the place of devils, so it is a blessing, and the right is more deserving of it. (Then he says) after exiting: (Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm by expelling the vile wastes which, if retained in the body, would make it ill. (And He gave me well-being) by preserving the essence of nutrition, because if it all exited, it would be destructive. And it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'Your forgiveness.' And they mentioned two interpretations: One is that he (peace be upon him) saw the abandonment of remembering Allah during his stay in the lavatory as a shortcoming from him, so he made up for it with Istighfar, for he used to remember Allah in all his states. The second is that Istighfar here is a metaphor for acknowledging the inability to fulfil the due of giving thanks for the blessing of feeding and nurturing the food from the time of consumption to the time of digestion and facilitating the exit of harm, with the safety of the body from pains, so he resorted to Istighfar, admitting the shortcoming of gratitude for the blessings.
(1) His statement: (And he should not remember Allah, etc.) Rather, it is disliked to speak absolutely while relieving oneself and during intercourse, except for a need that would be lost if delayed, such as warning a blind person about falling. His statement: (So he should not say 'Alhamdulillah' if he sneezes, etc.) He may do that in his heart without uttering it with his tongue. His statement: (And he should not look at his private part) For that is contrary to good manners, and similarly it is better for spouses not to look at each other's private parts. And just as covering is recommended for him, so is covering his head and lowering his voice. 'Ali said: Whoever looks excessively at his private part is punished with forgetfulness. And it is said: Whoever touches it excessively is afflicted with adultery. His statement: (Nor at what comes out) For it causes forgetfulness and is legally filthy, and there is no need for it. His statement: (Nor should he spit) because it yellows the teeth. His statement: (Nor should he blow his nose) due to filling his nose with a bad smell. His statement: (Nor should he turn around excessively, etc.) Because it is a place where devils are present, so one should not do anything unnecessary there. His statement: (Nor should he raise his eyes to the sky) because it is a place for reflecting on its signs, and this is not its place. His statement: (For it causes hemorrhoids and liver pain) That is related from Luqman the Wise, and because it is a place of devils, so it is recommended to hasten exiting from it. (2) Hemorrhoid: a thick fold of mucous membrane at the bottom of the anal fissure. Plural (hemorrhoids). And hemorrhoids are generally called a disease that causes varicose veins in the anus, commonly under the mucous membrane. Al-Mu'jam al-Wasit / bsr /. (3) Narrated by Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter on what a man says when he exits the lavatory (30), and al-Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter: What he says when he exits the lavatory (7).
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (Sharh) on Nur al-Idah, explaining the disliked and recommended actions when relieving oneself. The author begins by listing several makruhat (disliked actions): facing the sun or moon directly, because they are great signs of Allah and deserve respect; facing the direction of the wind, because the impurity may blow back; urinating or defecating in water, even flowing water, and similarly near a large body of water; in a shade that people use; in a hole (any animal hole) due to possible harm to the creature or oneself; on a road or in a cemetery, citing the hadith of the 'two curses'—the one who relieves himself in people's path or their shade; under a fruit-bearing tree because the fruit becomes impure; and urinating while standing, unless one has an excuse like back pain. The author then mentions it is disliked to urinate in a place where one later performs wudu or ghusl, as it causes waswasa (obsessive whispers). Then the recommendable (mustahabb) acts: entering the lavatory with a different garment from the salah garment, and protecting one's clothes from impurity and used water. It is disliked to enter with a ring containing Allah's name or Quranic verses. One should not uncover his private part while standing. One should not engage in dhikr (remembrance of Allah), so one does not praise Allah for sneezing, thank a sneezer, return greetings, or respond to the adhan while relieving oneself. One should not look at one's private part or at the excrement. One should not spit, blow nose, clear throat, turn excessively, or fidget. When exiting, one should step out with the right foot, praising Allah for removing harm and granting well-being (the du'a 'Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba 'anni al-adha wa 'afani). The author also mentions the Prophet's du'a 'Ghufranak' (Your forgiveness) and provides two interpretations: first, that the Prophet felt he had fallen short in dhikr during his stay and sought forgiveness, and second, that it is an admission of the inability to fully thank Allah for the blessings of digestion and expulsion. The commentary also includes additional notes from super-commentary, such as the permissibility of speaking when necessary (like warning a blind person) and the recommendation to cover the head and lower voice.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khalā'): The lavatory or place for relieving oneself.
الوسوسة (al-waswasah): Whisperings or obsessive thoughts from Shaytan, especially related to purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Say 'Alhamdulillah' only.
B) Say 'Alhamdulillah alladhi adhhaba anni al-adha wa afani'.
C) Say 'Ghufranak'.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic guidance for the lavatory includes specific words and actions that purify both body and soul.

Etiquette of Leaving the Lavatory
Rulings on exiting the lavatory and supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions and prohibitions when exiting the lavatory, and explain the Hanafi evidence and interpretation for the supplication.

Core Idea
Exiting with the right foot and reciting the supplication are sunnah, based on prophetic practice and interpretive reasoning.

This lesson covers the sunnah actions and makruh prohibitions related to leaving the lavatory. You will learn the specific etiquettes, the hadith evidence, and the scholarly interpretations behind the recommended supplication. Understanding these rulings helps you follow the Prophet's practice and avoid disliked behaviors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended and prohibited actions
Read the passage and list the sunnah actions (exiting with right foot, saying the supplication) and the makruh actions (raising gaze to sky, prolonged sitting).
The passage also includes other etiquettes from the commentary: no speech, no looking at private parts, etc.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The text cites the Prophet's saying 'Ghufranak' (Your forgiveness) as a supplication upon exiting. This hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi, and is a hadith ahad, making it zanni in transmission and meaning.
The hadith is used to derive the sunnah, not obligation.
3
Examine the commentator's expansion
The sharh offers two interpretations for 'Ghufranak': (1) compensation for the lack of dhikr inside the lavatory, and (2) acknowledgment of inability to fully thank Allah for the blessing of digestion and waste removal.
This expansion shows how the sunnah is enriched through scholarly reflection.
4
Determine the ruling levels
Based on the hadith and reasoning, the positive actions are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) and the prohibitions are makruh tanzih (disliked). No action is wajib or haram.
The Hanafi position is that these etiquettes are recommended, not obligatory.

Commentary
This passage from the sharh expands on the rulings of leaving the lavatory. It begins with the sunnah of exiting with the right foot, contrasting with entering with the left, because the right is associated with blessings and the left with impurities and devils. The supplication after exiting includes thanking Allah for removing harmful waste and preserving beneficial nourishment, with an additional report of the Prophet saying 'Ghufranaka' (Your forgiveness). The commentator offers two interpretations: first, the Prophet compensated for the lack of remembrance during his stay; second, it is an acknowledgment of inability to sufficiently thank Allah for the digestive process. The commentary also lists other etiquettes: speech is disliked, sneezing praise should be internal, looking at private parts is discouraged, and raising the gaze or prolonged sitting is harmful. These are based on transmitted wisdom and legal reasoning.

Key Terms
الخَلاء (al-khala'): The place used for relieving oneself; refers to the lavatory or toilet.
الأذى (al-adha): Harm or impurity; here specifically refers to the waste products and harmful substances.
الباسور (al-basur): Hemorrhoids; a medical condition of the anal region.

The First Pillar of Wudu: Washing the Face – Definition and Dispute
Definition of the first pillar and the meaning of washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the face in wudu, explain the dispute among Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the requirement of dripping (taqattur), and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Washing the face requires water to flow and drip – mere flow without dripping is insufficient per the soundest Hanafi view.

In this lesson, we examine the first pillar of wudu: washing the face. The author begins with the definition of wudu, then moves to its pillars. The Quranic command 'Wash your faces' establishes this obligation. However, what exactly constitutes 'washing'? Within the Hanafi school, there is a significant dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other regarding whether water must drip from the limb. We will unpack this ikhtilaf and see which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing the face during wudu. What is the hukm level? The text states it is one of the pillars (rukn) and fard (obligatory). Identify that it is fard 'ayn based on the Quran and ijma.
In Hanafi usul, a rukn is what the act stands upon; its omission invalidates the act entirely.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: the Quranic verse {Wash your faces} from Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6. This is a direct command (amr).
Also consider the broader meaning: the sharh uses the imperative to prove obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the command proves obligation. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah to the contrary. The verse has no such qarinah, so washing the face is fard.
This is a standard usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on the definition of ghusl
The sharh explains the dispute on what 'washing' (ghusl) requires. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say water must flow and drip (taqattur), even a single drop. Abu Yusuf says flowing (isal) without dripping suffices. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: validity of wudu in cases of minimal water usage.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, not a cross-madhhab one. The author cites Al-Fayd where the minimum is set at two drops as the soundest.
5
Apply the tarjih and the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the requirement of dripping, with at least two drops for certainty. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and later works adopt this. As a mufti, you would require dripping.
The face is also defined in length: from the hairline (forehead surface) to the chin. The width is discussed elsewhere. This passage is incomplete on the full boundaries.

Chapter on the Rulings of Ablution. The pillars of wudu are four, and they are its obligations. The first: washing the face, and its limit lengthwise: from the beginning of the surface of the forehead. Chapter on the Rulings of Ablution. With damm on the waw and fatḥa, it is a verbal noun, and with fatḥa only it is what one performs ablution with. In language it is derived from al-wada'a, which is beauty and cleanliness. It is said: wahuwa al-rajul, meaning he became beautiful. In sacred law it is specific cleanliness. It contains the linguistic meaning because it beautifies the limbs of ablution in this world by cleaning and in the Hereafter by blazonry, until it is said: the wisdom in washing these limbs is this meaning. For when a servant intends to serve a king, he must renew his cleanliness, and the easiest is purifying the limbs that are often exposed. When one sees them pure from dirt and clean from filth, the heart accepts them and the intellect approves them. Allah Almighty legislated for us a religion that He mentioned is the fitrah of Allah upon which He created mankind, so He legislated what they approve in their intellects and accept among themselves. And it is said otherwise. And he (the author) gave precedence to wudu over ghusl because Allah gave it precedence over it, and it has a cause, condition, ruling, pillar, and description. He began by explaining its pillar because it is the most important, and the pillar of a thing is that by which it stands. He said: (The pillars of wudu are four, and they are its obligations. The first of the pillars: washing the face) due to His saying the Exalted: {Wash your faces} [5:6] with fatḥa on the ghayn, a verbal noun from ghastu ghaslan, and with damm it is the noun, (3) (2) (3) and with kasr, what is used to wash with, such as marshmallow, soap, and the like. And al-ghusl is the flowing of water over the place such that it drips, even a drop according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), and according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) it suffices if it flows over the limb even if it does not drip. According to these two interpretations, rubbing is not included in its concept, but it is recommended as we shall mention, Allah willing. And in al-Fayd, dripping is shared in ghusl and is necessary, and its minimum is two drops as the soundest opinion, and mere flowing is not sufficient. And the face is what one faces with, i.e., what falls under sight when facing, and it is the mutual facing of two faces. (Its limit) i.e., the entirety of the face, lengthwise: from the beginning of the surface of the forehead, whether there is hair or not. And al-jabhah is the name for what touches the ground during prostration from an area above the eyebrows, i.e., the hairline.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage from the sharh introduces the chapter on wudu. It begins by defining wudu linguistically (derived from beauty/cleanliness) and legally (specific ritual purification). The author explains that the pillars of wudu are four, which are fard (obligatory). The first pillar is washing the face, supported by the Quranic verse {Wash your faces}. The commentator then clarifies the definition of 'ghusl' (washing): according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it requires water to flow over the limb such that it drips (even one drop suffices), while Abu Yusuf considers mere flowing sufficient without dripping. This difference does not include rubbing as part of the definition; rubbing is sunnah. The face is defined as what is seen when facing someone, and its length is measured from the beginning of the forehead (the hairline) to the chin. The forehead (jabhah) is the part that touches the ground in prostration, above the eyebrows. The passage is incomplete; the width and the lower boundary of the face are not mentioned here.

Key Terms
الوضوء (al-wudu'): Ritual purification by washing specific limbs with water, a prerequisite for salah.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing with water such that it flows over the limb; the minimal definition is disputed within the school.
الوجه (al-wajh): The face; what is seen when facing someone, including the forehead, cheeks, nose, mouth, chin, and the entire area from the hairline to the chin and between the ears.
التقاطر (al-taqattur): Dripping; water falling off the limb as a result of washing.
الإسالة (al-isalah): Flowing; water moving over the limb without necessarily dripping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the minimum requirement for water when washing the face in wudu?
A) Water must touch the face.
B) Water must flow over the face and drip, at least one drop (two drops for certainty).
C) Water must flow over the face, but dripping is not necessary.
D) Water must be poured from a vessel without specifying flow.

Key Takeaway
Washing the face is the first fard of wudu and requires water to flow and drip, with the mufta bihi requiring at least two drops, while mere flowing without dripping is insufficient for validity.

Definition of Wudu and the First Pillar: Washing the Face
Defines wudu legally and explains the first pillar with limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal definition of wudu, identify the limits of the face, and apply the Hanafi ruling on washing the white area between the sideburn and ear.

Core Idea
Washing the face is fard: from hairline to chin, earlobe to earlobe, including the white area.

Wudu is a specific cleanliness that beautifies both in this world and the next. Its first pillar is washing the face, commanded by Allah in Surah al-Ma'idah. This lesson unpacks the precise limits of the face and the legal definition of 'washing' (ghusl), including a key difference within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define Wudu
Understand the linguistic and legal meanings of wudu. Note its derivation from 'wada'ah' (beauty) and the legal definition as a specific cleanliness.
The author mentions that wudu beautifies limbs in this world through cleaning and in the hereafter by the blaze (tahjil).
2
Identify the First Pillar and Its Proof
Recognize that washing the face is the first of four pillars (fard). The proof is the Quranic verse: 'So wash your faces.' The imperative indicates obligation.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
3
Define the Legal Term 'Ghusl'
Ghusl is the flowing of water over the limb such that it drips (or at least flows, according to Abu Yusuf). Note that rubbing is sunnah, not an integral part of ghusl.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require dripping; Abu Yusuf suffices with flow. The relied-upon view requires dripping.
4
Memorize the Limits of the Face
Lengthwise: from the top of the forehead (hairline) to the bottom of the chin. Widthwise: between the lobes of the ears. The ears themselves are not part of the face.
The limits are exclusive; the hair on the forehead does not change the starting point.
5
Resolve the Dispute on the White Area
The white area between the sideburn (al-'idhar) and the ear falls within the width limit. The relied-upon position (sahih) is that it must be washed, contrary to Abu Yusuf's view after beard growth.
The author explicitly states 'wa huwa al-sahih', indicating the tarjih.

فصل في أحكام الوضوء بضم الواو وفتحها، مصدر، وبفتحها فقط: ما يتوضأ به، وهو في اللغة مأخوذ من الوضاءة، وهي الحُسْنُ والنظافة. يقال: وَهُوَ الرجل، أي صار وضيئاً وشرعاً نظافة مخصوصة. ففيه المعنى اللغوي، لأنه يُحَسِّن أعضاء الوضوء في الدنيا بالتنظيف، وفي الآخرة بالتحجيل. وقيل غير ذلك، وقدم على الغسل، لأن الله تعالى قدمه عليه، وله سبب، وشرط، وحكم، وركن، وصفة بدأ ببيان ركنه، لأنه الأهم، وركن الشيء ما قام به، فقال: (أركان الوضوء أربعة، وهي فرائضه الأوّلُ من الأركان: غَسْلُ الوجه) لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ﴾ بفتح الغين، مصدر غسلت غسلاً، وبالضم الاسم، وبالكسر ما يغسل به من خطمي وصابون ونحوه. والغَسل إسالة الماء على المحل، بحيث يتقاطر، ولو قطرة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله، وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يجزئ إذا سال على العضو، وإن لم يقطر. فعلى هذين التفسيرين لا يكون الدَّلك من مفهومه، ولكنه مندوب كما سنذكره. وفي « الفيض» يشترك التقاطر في الغسل، ولابد، وأقله قطرتان في الأصح، ولا يكفي الإسالة، والوجه ما يواجه به الإنسان، أي ما وقع عليه النظر عند المواجهة، وهي تقابل الوجهين. (وحده) أي: جملة الوجه، طُولاً : مِنْ مَبْدَأ سَطْحِ الجَبْهَةِ) سواء كان عليه شعر أو لم يكن، والجبهة : اسم لما يصيب الأرض حالة السجود مما فوق الحاجبين، أي: منابت الشعر، إلى أسفل الذقن، وحده عَرْضاً ما بين شحمتي الأذنين، ويقال فيها أيضاً: ما اكتنفه الجبينان، فيغسل من ابتداء الجبهة إلى أسفل الذقن وهي: مجتمع لحييه، واللحي: منبت اللحية والعظم الذي عليه الأسنان. (وَحَدُّهُ) أي: الوجه (عَرْضاً) بفتح العين مقابل الطول، ما بين شحمتي الأُذُنَيْنِ) شحمتهما معلق القرط). والأذن بضمتين تخفف وتثقل، والحد المذكور يشير إلى أن الغاية ليست داخلة لا في الطول ولا في العرض. ويشمل الحد البياض الذي بين العذار والأذن، فليلزم غسله، وهو الصحيح. وعن أبي يوسف لا يلزم غسله بعد نبات اللحية.
Chapter on the rulings of wudu. Wudu with dammah or fatha on the waw is a verbal noun, and with fatha only it means the water used for wudu. Linguistically it is derived from wada'ah (beauty and cleanliness). It is said: 'wahuwara rajulun' meaning he became handsome. Legally it is a specific cleanliness. It contains the linguistic meaning because it beautifies the limbs of wudu in this world through cleaning, and in the hereafter through the blaze (on the Day of Resurrection). ... The pillars of wudu are four, which are its obligations: the first: washing the face, due to His statement: 'So wash your faces.' ... Washing is the flowing of water over the body part such that it drips, even one drop according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf it suffices if it flows over the limb even if it does not drip. Rubing is not part of the concept but is recommended. The face is what one faces others with, and its limit lengthwise from the beginning of the surface of the forehead, whether there is hair or not, to the bottom of the chin, and widthwise between the lobes of the ears. The limit includes the white area between the sideburn and the ear, so it must be washed; this is the correct view. Abu Yusuf narrates that it is not necessary to wash it after the beard grows.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the first pillar of wudu: washing the face. The commentary begins by defining the term 'wudu' linguistically and legally, then explains why the author started with the arkan (pillars) rather than other elements. It provides the Quranic proof (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) and then elaborates on the legal definition of 'ghasl' (washing). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider dripping as necessary, while Abu Yusuf holds that mere flow suffices. The face's limits are clearly defined: from the top of the forehead to the bottom of the chin (including the beard area) in length, and from ear lobe to ear lobe in width. An important subtlety is the inclusion of the white area between the sideburn (al-'idhar) and the ear; the author affirms it must be washed, though there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that after the beard grows it is no longer required—but the relied-upon position is that it must be washed. The commentary also notes that the mentioned limits exclude the ears themselves, as the ears are not part of the face for washing purposes.

Key Terms
الوضوء (al-wudu): Legally a specific cleanliness performed with water on specific limbs.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Flowing water over the body part such that it drips (or at least flows according to Abu Yusuf).
الوجه (al-wajh): The face: from the top of the forehead (hairline) to the chin, and from ear lobe to ear lobe.
الذقن (al-dhaqan): The chin, the bottom limit of the face lengthwise.
شحمتا الأذنين (shahmata al-udhnayn): The earlobes (literally the fatty parts of the ears), used as the widthwise limit of the face.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Washing the face is fard, with defined limits from forehead to chin and earlobe to earlobe, including the white area between sideburn and ear.

The Second, Third, and Fourth Pillars of Wudu
Details the washing of hands and feet and wiping the head with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three pillars of wudu (washing hands to elbows, feet to ankles, wiping a quarter of the head), identify their Qur'anic and hadith proofs, and explain the Hanafi position on the inclusion of elbows and ankles and the required amount for wiping the head.

Core Idea
Washing to the elbows and ankles is fard; wiping one quarter of the head is sufficient in Hanafi wudu.

In this lesson, we examine three essential pillars of wudu: washing the hands including elbows, washing the feet including ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head. The Hanafi school derives these obligations from clear Qur'anic and hadith evidence, and the passage addresses important linguistic and fiqhi debates, such as the inclusion of the ankles (against Zufar) and the sufficiency of wiping a quarter of the head (based on prophetic practice). Understanding these pillars is critical for the validity of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three pillars
The passage explicitly names the second, third, and fourth pillars: washing hands with elbows, washing feet with ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head.
These are arkan of wudu.
2
Analyze the proof for washing hands and feet
The verse (5:6) is cited; note the grammatical argument that 'ila' includes the limit, and the accusative case indicates washing.
The accusative reading of 'arjulakum' confirms washing, not wiping.
3
Examine the debate on ankle inclusion
Zufar's view that ankles are not included is mentioned; the passage counters by stating that the preposition includes the limit and references longer works for the full refutation.
The majority Hanafi position includes the ankles.
4
Evaluate the proof for wiping a quarter of the head
Hadith of Anas and 'Ata' are cited; note that even mursal hadith are acceptable in Hanafi school for this purpose, establishing the obligation of at least a quarter.
The minimum is a quarter; the Sunnah is to wipe the entire head.
5
Apply the rulings
Understand the practical consequence: failure to wash elbows/ankles or wipe at least a quarter of the head invalidates wudu.
Consult a mufti for specific edge cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: غَسل يديه مع مرفقيه لقوله تعالى: وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ أحد المرفقين بعبارة النص، لأن مقابلة الجمع بالجمع تقتضي مقابلة الأفراد بالأفراد، والآخر بدلالته لتساويهما وعدم الأولوية، وللإجماع على فرضية غسل المرفقين. والمرفق بكسر الميم وفتح الفاء، وقلبه لغة - ملتقى عظم العضد وعظم الذراع. وَالركن الثالث: غَسْلُ رِجْلَيْهِ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ بالنص، عطفاً على وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام بعدما غسل رجليه: «هَذَا وُضُوءٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ الله الصَّلاةَ إِلا به». والجر للمجاورة، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُورُ عِينٌ على قراءة الجر. مَع كَعْبَيْهِ لدخول الغاية مع المغيا عند المحققين والجواب عن خلاف زفر في المطولات، والكعبان هما: العظمان الناتئان من جانبي القدم المرتفعان، والاشتقاق يدل على الارتفاع، ومنه الكاعب: وهي الجارية التي يبدو ثديها للنهود، ومنه الكعبة البيت الحرام لارتفاعها عن سائر البيوت. وَالركن الرابع: مَسْحُ رَبعِ رأسه. لقول أنس: رَأَيْتُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَتَوَضَاً وعَليهِ عَمَامَةٌ قطرية، فأدخل يده مِنْ تَحْتِ العَمَامَةِ، فَمَسَحَ مقدَّمَ رَأْسِهِ. وقول عطاء: أنه توضأ فحسر العَمَامَةِ وَمَسَحَ مقدم رأسه أو قال: ناصيته، فإنه حجة عندنا.
And the second: washing his two hands along with his elbows, due to the Qur'anic verse: وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ. One of the two elbows is mentioned explicitly in the text because when a plural is used in contrast to a plural it implies each individual corresponds to its counterpart, and the other elbow is implied by necessity due to their equality and lack of priority, and there is consensus on the obligation of washing the elbows. The elbow is the joint of the upper arm bone and forearm bone. And the third pillar: washing his two feet, due to the Qur'anic verse: وَأَرْجُلَكُم explicitly, as an accusative coordinate of وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ. And due to the Prophet's statement after washing his feet: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' The genitive case is due to adjacency, like in the verse وَحُورٌ عِينٌ in the reading with jarr. Together with his two ankles, because the extent is included with the extended object according to the verifying scholars, and the response to Zufar's disagreement in the lengthy works. The two ankles are the two protruding bones on the sides of the foot, elevated; etymology indicates elevation, from which is kā'ib (a girl whose breasts begin to swell) and Ka'bah for its elevation above other houses. And the fourth pillar: wiping a quarter of his head. Due to the statement of Anas: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudu while wearing a Qatari turban, so he inserted his hand under the turban and wiped his forehead.' And the statement of 'Ata': 'He performed wudu and uncovered his turban and wiped his forehead' or 'his forelock,' and it is a proof for us.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage covers the remaining three pillars of wudu. The second pillar is washing the hands including the elbows. The commentary explains that the Qur'anic command to wash 'your hands up to the elbows' includes both elbows by necessity and consensus. The third pillar is washing the feet including the ankles. The text addresses a grammatical issue: the word 'your feet' (arjulakum) could be read in the accusative (indicating washing) or genitive (indicating wiping). The author affirms that the reading is accusative, coordinated with 'your hands', showing washing is required. The phrase 'with his two ankles' indicates that the ankles are included in the washing, countering Zufar's view that only the feet (without the ankles) need to be washed. The fourth pillar is wiping a quarter of the head. The proof comes from hadith of Anas and 'Ata', showing the Prophet wiped part of his head. The commentary notes that even if the hadith are mursal (in the case of 'Ata'), such reports are acceptable as evidence in the Hanafi school for specifying the amount.

Key Terms
المرفق (al-mirfaq): The elbow joint: the meeting point of the upper arm bone (al-'adud) and forearm bone (al-dhira').
الكعب (al-ka'b): The ankle bone: the protruding bone on each side of the foot at the junction of the leg and foot.
المسح (al-mash): Wiping; passing a wet hand over the head (or other body part).
ربع الرأس (rub' al-ra's): One quarter of the head; the minimum amount required to be wiped for wudu according to Hanafi school.
الناصية (al-nasiyah): The forelock; the front part of the scalp.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The front part only
D) The whole head or any part thereof

Key Takeaway
Washing the hands to the elbows, feet to the ankles, and wiping at least a quarter of the head are obligatory pillars of wudu according to the Hanafi school.

The Four Fard Acts of Wudu
States the four fard acts of wudu with definitions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four fard acts of wudu, identify the Quranic proof and its Hanafi interpretation, and explain the Hanafi ruling on the extent of wiping the head and washing the whiteness near the ear.

Core Idea
The four fard acts of wudu are washing face, hands to elbows, feet to ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head.

Wudu is the key to prayer; knowing exactly what Allah has made obligatory ensures our worship is valid. This lesson unpacks the four fard acts as defined by the Hanafi school, with proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. We will also examine a subtle ikhtilaf about the face's boundary and the head's wiping requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four fard acts
List the four acts: washing face, washing hands to elbows, washing feet to ankles, wiping a quarter of the head. Note that the face includes from hairline to chin and between the earlobes.
The text also mentions the 'whiteness between sideburn and ear' as part of the face.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil naqli)
The Quranic verse (Al-Ma'ida 5:6) is the main textual evidence. Observe the imperative 'faghsilu' (wash) which indicates obligation, and the particle 'ila' (to) which, in Hanafi usul, includes the limit (elbows and ankles) in the wash.
The verse also commands wiping the head, but the exact amount is clarified by the Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for each act
For the face: the verse orders washing 'your faces' without a limit, so the definition comes from the Sunnah and customary understanding. For the hands and feet: 'ila' includes the joints (elbows, ankles). For the head: the 'bi' in 'bi ru'usikum' indicates partiality, and ahad hadith specify a quarter.
The text dismisses the view that three fingers' width suffices for head wiping as baseless (not conceivable naratively or rationally).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (intra- and inter-madhhab)
Intra-Hanafi: Abu Yusuf held that after the beard grows, the whiteness between sideburn and ear need not be washed; the correct view (sahih) is that it must be washed. Inter-madhhab: Shafi'is require wiping the entire head; Hanafis require only a quarter.
The Hanafi response on head wiping relies on ahad hadith (Anas and 'Ata) which they accept for specifying the amount.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and operative ruling
The text clearly states the correct view is that the whiteness must be washed, and the mufta bihi for head wiping is a quarter. The three-finger view is dismissed. Thus, in practice, a Hanafi must ensure all four acts are performed as defined.
If water or rain reaches the obligatory amount, it suffices; the tool (hand) is only meant for delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۳)
ويقال فيها أيضاً: ما اكتنفه الجبينان، فيغسل من ابتداء الجبهة (إلى أسفل الذقنِ) وهي: مجتمع لحييه، واللحي: منبت اللحية والعظم الذي عليه الأسنان. وسنذكر (۱) حكم اللحية إن شاء الله تعالى. (وَحَدُّهُ) أي: الوجه (عَرْضاً) بفتح العين مقابل الطول، ما بين شحمتي الأُذُنَيْنِ) شحمتهما معلق القرط). والأذن بضمتين تخفف وتثقل، والحد المذكور يشير إلى أن الغاية ليست داخلة لا في الطول ولا في العرض. ويشمل الحد البياض الذي بين العذار ) والأذن، فليلزم غسله، وهو الصحيح. وعن أبي يوسف لا يلزم غسله بعد نبات اللحية. (و) الركن ( الثَّانِي: غَسْلُ يَدَيْهِ مَعَ مِرْفَقَيْهِ) لقوله تعالى: وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ الثالة : ٦] أحد المرفقين بعبارة النص، لأن مقابلة الجمع بالجمع تقتضي مقابلة الأفراد بالأفراد، والآخر بدلالته لتساويهما وعدم الأولوية، وللإجماع على فرضية غسل المرفقين. والمرفق بكسر الميم وفتح الفاء، وقلبه لغة - ملتقى عظم العضد وعظم الذراع. (وَ) الركن ( الثَّالث: غَسْلُ رِجْلَيْهِ) لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَرْجُلَكُم الثالة : ٦] بالنص. عطفاً على وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام بعدما غسل رجليه: «هَذَا وُضُوءٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ الله الصَّلاةَ إِلا به ). والجر للمجاورة، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُورُ عِينٌ [الواقعة : ٢٢]. على قراءة الجر. (مَع كَعْبَيْهِ) لدخول الغاية مع المغيا عند المحققين والجواب عن خلاف زفر في المطولات والكعبــان هما: العظمان الناتئان من جانبي القدم المرتفعان، والاشتقاق يدل على الارتفاع، ومنه الكاعب: وهـي الجارية التي يبدو ثديها للنهود، ومنه الكعبة البيت الحرام لارتفاعها عن سائر البيوت. (و) الركن الرابع: مَسْحُ رَبع رأسهِ). لقول أنس: ( رَأَيْتُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَتَوَضَاً وعَليهِ عَمَامَةٌ قطرية، فأدخل يده مِنْ تَحْتِ العَمَامَةِ، فَمَسَحَ مقدَّمَ رَأْسِهِ ). وقول عطاء: «أنه توضاً فحسرَ العَمَامَةِ وَمَسَحَ مقدم ا و إن كان مرسلاً، وخبر الآحاد صالح لبيــان المـقـدار رأسه أو قال: «ناصيته ) (۱) فإنه حجة عندنا
(٤)
مراد بالآية، وأما تقدير المفروض بثلاثة أصابع فهو غير متصور رواية ودراية، فلا يعمل به وإن صحح، ومحل المسح ما فوق الأذنين، فلو مسح على شعره أجزأه، بخلاف ما لو كانت ذؤابتاه )
(۲)
مشدودتين على رأسه فمسح على أعلاهما فإنه لا يصح . والمسح لغة: إمـرار الـيـد عـلـى الشـيء، وإصطلاحاً: إصابة اليد المبتلة العضو ولو بعد غسل العضو، لا مسحه. ولا ببلل أُخِذ من عضو، والآلة لم تقصد إلا للإيصال، فإذا أصابه ماء أو مطر قدر المفروض أجزأه.
To the bottom of the chin; its width is between the earlobes. The second: washing his hands together with his elbows. The third: washing his feet together with his ankles. The fourth: wiping a quarter of his head. It is also said about it: what is enclosed by the two foreheads; so he washes from the beginning of the forehead to the bottom of the chin, which is the meeting point of his jaws. The jaw is the place of growth of the beard and the bone on which the teeth are. We will mention the ruling of the beard if Allah wills. (And its limit) meaning the face (width) with a fatha on the 'ayn, opposite length, (is between the earlobes) their fat is where the earring hangs. The ear (udhun) with two dammas, light and heavy. The mentioned limit indicates that the extremity is not included, neither in length nor in width. The limit includes the whiteness between the sideburn and the ear, so it is necessary to wash it, and this is correct. From Abu Yusuf it is not necessary to wash it after the beard has grown. (And) the second pillar: washing his hands together with his elbows, due to His statement: 'and your hands to the elbows' [al-Ma'ida:6]. One of the elbows by the wording of the text, because the matching of a plural with a plural necessitates the matching of individuals with individuals, and the other by implication due to their equality and lack of priority, and due to consensus on the obligation of washing the elbows. The elbow (mirfaq) with kasr of the meem and fatha of the fa, and its inversion in language is the meeting point of the bone of the upper arm and the bone of the forearm. (And) the third pillar: washing his feet, due to His statement: 'and your feet' [al-Ma'ida:6] by the text, as a conjunction to 'and your hands'. And due to his statement, peace be upon him, after he washed his feet: 'This is an ablution without which Allah does not accept prayer.' The genitive is for adjacency, like His statement: 'and beautiful-eyed maidens' [al-Waqi'a:22] in the reading with genitive. (Together with his ankles) because the extremity is included with the included according to the verifiers, and the answer to the disagreement of Zafr is in the lengthy works. The two ankles are the two prominent bones on the sides of the foot, elevated; the derivation indicates elevation, from it is 'ka'ab' meaning the young girl whose breast begins to appear due to swelling, and from it is 'Ka'ba' the Sacred House for its elevation above other houses. (And) the fourth pillar: wiping a quarter of his head, due to the saying of Anas: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, performing ablution while wearing a Qatri turban; he inserted his hand under the turban and wiped the front of his head.' And the saying of 'Ata: 'He performed ablution, uncovered his turban, and wiped the front of his head or his forelock' even if it is mursal, and ahad reports are valid for clarifying the amount meant by the verse. As for the estimation of the obligatory as three fingers, it is not conceivable narratively or rationally, so it is not acted upon even if it is sahih. The place of wiping is above the ears; so if he wipes over his hair, it suffices him, contrary to if he has two braids tied on his head and he wipes over their tops, then it is not valid. Wiping linguistically is passing the hand over something, and terminologically it is the contact of the wet hand with the limb, even after washing the limb, not its wiping. And not with moisture taken from another limb, and the tool is only meant for delivery; so if water or rain reaches him in the obligatory amount, it suffices him.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the four obligatory (fard) acts of wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author defines each act precisely, providing proof from the Quran and Sunnah. The face is defined from the hairline to the chin, width between earlobes; the hands include the elbows; the feet include the ankles; and a quarter of the head must be wiped. The text supports the Hanafi position that wiping a quarter is sufficient, relying on a hadith of Anas (ra) and the mursal report of 'Ata. It dismisses the view that only three fingers' width is required as baseless. It also clarifies that washing the whiteness between the sideburn and ear is necessary (the correct view), though Abu Yusuf held it is not required after the beard grows. The passage emphasizes that the extremities (elbows and ankles) are included in the wash due to the Quranic particle 'ila' which, according to the Hanafis, includes the limit. The author refutes the Shafi'i view that wiping the whole head is obligatory, arguing that a quarter is proven by the sunnah.

Key Terms
فَرْض (fard): An obligatory act that must be performed; its omission invalidates the act of worship.
مِرْفَق (mirfaq): Elbow joint where upper arm and forearm meet; must be washed in wudu.
كَعْب (ka'b): Ankle bone: the two prominent bones on the sides of the foot.
مَسْح (mas'h): Wiping: passing wet hand over a limb; for the head, it is passing wet hand over a quarter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How much of the head must be wiped to fulfill the fard in wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) The entire head
B) A quarter of the head
C) Three fingers' width
D) The front part only

Key Takeaway
The four fard acts of wudu are washing the face, hands to elbows, feet to ankles, and wiping a quarter of the head; omitting any of these invalidates wudu.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Conditions of Obligation and Validity of Wudu
Defines the cause, ruling, and conditions for wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sabab of wudu, list the eight conditions for its obligation, and identify the three conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Wudu becomes obligatory only when eight precise conditions are met; its validity requires three further conditions.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah introduces the foundational concepts for understanding wudu in Hanafi fiqh. Before studying the actions of wudu, one must know what triggers its obligation (sabab), when it becomes obligatory (shurut al-wujub), and what makes it valid (shurut al-sihha). This lesson unpacks these elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab and hukm of wudu
The sabab (cause) is the intention to perform an act that is not permissible without purification, such as salah. The worldly hukm is that it makes such acts permissible; the otherworldly hukm is reward.
In Hanafi usul, sabab is distinct from ‘illa; it is a sign that leads to the obligation.
2
List the eight conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub)
These are: sanity (al-‘aql), puberty (al-bulugh), Islam (al-Islam), ability to use sufficient pure water (al-qudra ‘ala isti‘mal al-ma’ al-kafi), presence of hadath (state of impurity), absence of menstruation (al-hayd) and postpartum bleeding (al-nifas), and constriction of time (diq al-waqt).
The condition of diq al-waqt is uniquely Hanafi; without it, wudu for a future prayer is not obligatory.
3
Understand the unique condition: constriction of time
This means when a prayer time is about to expire, it becomes wajib to immediately perform wudu and pray. If time is expansive, wudu for that prayer is not obligatory.
This condition is debated among schools; Shafi‘is do not list it.
4
Note the three conditions for validity (shurut al-sihha)
The passage says there are three conditions for validity but does not list them. According to the commentary, they effectively require using water that is tahur (purifying) and ensuring that water reaches the skin without any impediment.
These conditions are detailed in other chapters.
5
Distinguish conditions of obligation from conditions of validity
A condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) must be present for the act to be required; if absent, the act is not obligatory. A condition of validity (shart al-sihha) must be present for the act to be legally sound; if absent, the act is invalid.
Example: an insane person is not obligated to perform wudu, but if a sane person performs wudu without water reaching the skin, it is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسببه: استباحة ما لا يَحِلُّ إلا به، وهو حكمه الدنيوي وحكمُهُ الأخروي: النواب في الآخرة. وشَرْطُ وجوبه: العقل، والبلوغ، والإسلام، وقُدْرَةٌ على استعمال الماء الكافي، ووجود الحَدَثِ، وعدم الحيض والنفاس، وضيق الوقتِ. وشرط صحتِه ثلاثة.

(۱) الذوائب: جمع ذؤابة وهي الشعر المضفور من شعر الرأس. النهاية (١٥١/٢). (۲) أي: التي أديرت ملفوفة على الرأس بحيث لو أرخاها لكانت مسترسلة. ط.
- ٦٢ -
And its cause: making permissible that which is not permissible except by it; and this is its worldly ruling, and its otherworldly ruling: reward in the hereafter. And the conditions of its obligation are eight: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient water, presence of hadath, absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and constriction of time. And the conditions of its validity are three.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage defines the cause (sabab) of wudu—which is the intention to perform an act that is prohibited without purification, such as prayer. The worldly ruling is that it makes such acts permissible; the otherworldly reward is thawab. Then it lists eight conditions for wudu to be obligatory (shurut al-wujub). These include: sanity (since the insane are not addressed), puberty (children are not obligated but their acts are valid), Islam (non-Muslims are not addressed with branches of shari'a), ability to use sufficient pure water (those unable are not obligated), presence of hadath (one must actually be impure), absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding (women in these states do not perform wudu for salah but must perform ghusl), and constriction of time (if a prayer is about to expire, it becomes wajib to perform wudu immediately; otherwise it is expansive). Some scholars count nine conditions. The author simplifies by saying: 'condition of obligation is the ability of the obligated person to perform purification with water.' Then it states that the conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha) are three, which essentially boil down to using water that is tahur (purifying) and ensuring it reaches the skin without any impediment. The brevity is for ease of teaching.

Key Terms
سَبَب (sabab): That which leads to something without affecting it; here, the intention to perform an act requiring purification.
شَرْطُ الْوُجُوب (shart al-wujub): Condition for an act to become obligatory; if absent, the act is not required.
حَدَث (hadath): State of ritual impurity that nullifies wudu; presence of hadath is a condition for obligation of wudu.
ضِيقُ الْوَقْت (diq al-waqt): When the time for an obligatory prayer is so short that it necessitates immediate wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of wudu according to the passage?
A) Sanity
B) Islam
C) Presence of water
D) Intention to pray

Key Takeaway
The obligation of wudu depends on eight specific conditions; its validity depends on three conditions including using pure water and ensuring it reaches the skin.

Taharah — Purification

The Cause and Conditions of Wudu
Commentary on cause, conditions of obligation and validity of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause (sabab) of wudu and list the eight conditions of obligation and three conditions of validity as taught in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wudu's cause: making lawful what is unlawful; obligation: eight conditions summarized as ability; validity: three conditions ensuring proper water contact.

In this lesson, we dissect the foundational legal structure of wudu from the Hanafi matn of Nur al-Idah. The passage clarifies what makes wudu obligatory and what ensures its validity. Understanding these conditions is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish cause from conditions
The cause (sabab) is the intended act that makes wudu necessary; the passage defines it as 'making lawful what is not lawful except by it'. Conditions (shurut) are external factors that must exist for obligation or validity.
The sabab does not directly effect the ruling; it is the reason the ruling applies.
2
Identify the eight conditions of obligation
The author lists: sanity, puberty, Islam, ability to use sufficient pure water, existence of hadath, absence of menstruation/postpartum bleeding, and narrowness of time. Some count nine, but the author summarizes all as 'ability to perform purification with water'.
Narrowness of time means the prayer time is about to end.
3
Identify the three conditions of validity
Validity depends on: (1) covering the skin with pure water, (2) cessation of anything that contradicts wudu (hadath, menses, postpartum during the act), and (3) removal of barriers like wax or fat.
These three reduce to one: ensuring no hindrance to water reaching the skin.
4
Differentiate obligation vs. validity
Obligation conditions determine when wudu is required; validity conditions determine whether a performed wudu counts. For example, a child may not be obligated but if they perform wudu correctly, it is valid.
Wudu can be performed without obligation (e.g., for refreshment).
5
Note the Hanafi stance on masah
The passage rejects that the obligatory wipe is limited to three fingers. It defines masah as touching the limb with a wet hand, not wiping away wetness. Wiping over hair suffices; over tight braids does not.
This clarifies a common cross-madhhab dispute.

المراد بالآية، وأما تقدير المفروض بثلاثة أصابع فهو غير متصور رواية ودراية، فلا يعمل به وإن صحح، ومحل المسح ما فوق الأذنين، فلو مسح على شعره أجزأه، بخلاف ما لو كانت ذؤابتاه مشدودتين على رأسه فمسح على أعلاهما فإنه لا يصح . والمسح لغة: إمـرار الـيـد عـلـى الشـيء، وإصطلاحاً: إصابة اليد المبتلة العضو ولو بعد غسل العضو، لا مسحه. ولا ببلل أُخِذ من عضو، والآلة لم تقصد إلا للإيصال، فإذا أصابه ماء أو مطر قدر المفروض أجزأه.
