8 min
The Ruling on Siwak: A Sunnah of Wudu
Explaining the sunnah status, time, and virtue of siwak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that siwak is a sunnah of wudu, state its virtue, and distinguish it from being a sunnah of prayer.

Core Idea
Siwak is a confirmed sunnah of wudu in the Hanafi school; its virtue extends to every prayer performed with that wudu.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text clearly establishes the ruling of siwak as a sunnah of wudu, not of prayer. It explains the recommended practice, the evidence from hadith, and the great reward. By studying this lesson, you will understand the basis for this ruling and how it impacts daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that siwak is classified as a sunnah (recommended) act. The passage states it is from the sunan of wudu in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'Siwak purifies the mouth and pleases the Lord' and the report that a prayer with siwak is superior to seventy prayers without it.
Both are zanni al-thubut but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Trace the legal classification
Understand why it is sunnah of wudu, not of prayer. The text explicitly says: 'siwak is from the sunan of wudu in our school, not from the sunan of prayer.' This distinction affects when the virtue is attained.
The virtue is attained with the wudu, not by repeating siwak at each prayer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider siwak a sunnah of prayer. The Hanafi school restricts it to wudu based on its analysis of the evidence.
This is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Understand the practical implication
The ruling means that using siwak once during wudu fulfills the sunnah for all prayers performed with that wudu, even if not used again at each prayer.
Siwak is also recommended in other states beyond wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ابتدائه، ولو بالإصْبَع عند فَقْدِهِ. أو « مَعَ كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ » ). ولما ورد « أنَّ كُلَّ صَلَاةٍ بِهِ تفضلُ سَبْعِينَ صَلاة بدونـه » . وينبغي أن يـكـون ليناً في غلط الإصبع، طول شبر مستوياً، قليل العقد من الأشجار المعروفة، وهي: الأراك، ليكون أقطع للبلغم، وأنقى للصدر، وأهني للطعام، وأن يستاك عرضاً، لا طولاً، لئلا يضـر لـحـم الأسـنان، وعليه الأكثر. وقال « الغزنوي » : يستاك طولاً وعرضاً ( في ابتدائـه)، أي الوضوء. ونص عليه، لأن الابتداء به سنة أيضاً. ووقته عند المضمضة على قول الأكثر. وقال غيرهم قبل الوضوء، والسواك من سنن الوضوء عندنا لا من سنن الصلاة، فيحصل فضيلته في كل صلاة صلاها بوضوء استاك فيـه مـن غير استياك عند قيامه لها. وليس السواك من خصائص الوضوء، فإنه يستحب في حالات، منها تغير الفم، والقيام من النوم، وإلى الصلاة، ودخول البيت واجتماع الناس، وقراءة القرآن والحديث، لقول أبي حنيفة: إن السواك من سنن الدين، فيستوي فيه الأحوال كلها. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: السَّوَاكُ مَطْهَرَةٌ لِلْفَمِ، مَرْضَاةٌ لِلرَّبِّ». وفضيلة السواك تحصل (وَلَو) كان الاستياك (بالإصبع)، أو خرقة خشنة (عند فقده)، أي: السواك أو فقد أسنانه، أو ضرر بفمه. لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: يُجْزِئُ مِنَ السَّوَاكِ الأصَابِعُ ). وقال علي : « التشويص) بالمسبحة والإبـهـام ســواك». ويقــوم العلك مقامه للنساء، لرقة بشرتهن ويستحب إمساكه باليد اليمني والسنة في كيفية أخذه، أن تجعل الخنصر من يمينك أسفل السواك، والبنصر والسبابة فوقه، واجعل الإبهام أسفل رأسه. كما رواه ابن مسعود ). ولا تقبض القبضة على السواك، فإنه يورث الباسور).
At the beginning of it (wudu), even if with the finger when it (siwak) is not found. Or 'with every prayer'. And it has been reported that 'every prayer with it is superior to seventy prayers without it.' And it should be soft, about the thickness of a finger, a span long, straight, with few knots, from known trees, namely the arak tree, to be most effective in cutting phlegm, purifying the chest, and promoting appetite. And one should use it widthwise, not lengthwise, lest it harm the gums. The majority are upon this. Al-Ghaznawi said: One should use it lengthwise and widthwise at its beginning, i.e., of wudu. And he stated it because beginning with it is also sunnah. Its time is at the time of rinsing the mouth according to the majority. Others said before wudu. Siwak is from the sunan of wudu in our school, not from the sunan of prayer; so its virtue is attained in every prayer performed with a wudu in which one used siwak, even without using siwak again when standing for it. Siwak is not specific to wudu; it is recommended in situations including: change of mouth odor, waking from sleep, going to prayer, entering the home, gathering with people, and reciting Quran and hadith, due to Abu Hanifa's statement: Siwak is from the sunan of the religion, so it is equal in all states. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Siwak purifies the mouth and pleases the Lord.' The virtue of siwak is attained even if one uses a finger or a rough cloth when it (siwak) is not found, or when one has lost teeth, or there is harm to his mouth, due to his saying: 'The fingers suffice for siwak.' And Ali said: 'Rubbing with the index finger and thumb is siwak.' Chewing gum takes its place for women due to the delicacy of their skin. It is recommended to hold it with the right hand. The sunnah in how to take it is to place your little finger of your right hand below the siwak, the ring finger and index finger above it, and place the thumb below its head, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. Do not grip the siwak with a full fist, for it causes hemorrhoids.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the rulings of siwak. It begins by stating that siwak is recommended at the start of wudu, and even with a finger if no twig is available. It cites a hadith that prayer with siwak is 70 times better. The preferred siwak is from arak, soft, a span long, straight, few knots. It should be used widthwise to avoid gum harm. Al-Ghaznawi added that it should be used both lengthwise and widthwise at the start of wudu. The time for siwak according to most scholars is during mouth rinsing (madmadah), others say before wudu. Importantly, in the Hanafi school, siwak is a sunnah of wudu, not of prayer. This means its virtue is achieved as long as one used siwak during wudu, even if not repeated for the prayer. Siwak is not restricted to wudu; it is recommended in many situations. Abu Hanifa considered it a sunnah of the religion, applicable in all states. The hadith 'siwak purifies the mouth' is cited. Even if one cannot use a twig, using a finger or rough cloth attains the virtue. For women, gum chewing is a substitute. The proper method of holding is described: little finger below, ring and index above, thumb below the head. Grip should not be a full fist as it causes hemorrhoids.

Key Terms
السواك (al-siwāk): A twig used for cleaning teeth, specifically from the arak tree, as per this text.
التشويص (al-tashwīṣ): Rubbing the teeth with the finger, as a substitute for siwak.
العلك (al-‘ilk): Chewing gum, used as a substitute for siwak for women due to delicate skin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary association of the sunnah of siwak?
A) It is a sunnah of prayer specifically.
B) It is a sunnah of wudu, extending to any prayer performed with that wudu.
C) It is a sunnah of fasting.
D) It is a sunnah of reciting Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Siwak is a sunnah of wudu in the Hanafi school, not of prayer, and its great reward is attained with a wudu performed with siwak.

Method and Substitutes of Siwak: Practical Guidelines
Detailing substitutes for siwak and the proper method of holding it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct method of using siwak and identify valid substitutes when siwak is not available.

Core Idea
The virtue of siwak is attained even with finger rubbing or a rough cloth; women may use chewing gum due to delicate skin.

This part of the passage focuses on the practical aspects of siwak: what to do when a twig is not available, and the correct way to hold and use it. You will learn the Prophetic guidance on substitutions and the proper grip of the miswak, including a warning against gripping it like a fist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the substitutes for siwak
The passage states that the virtue is attained even with a finger or a rough cloth if siwak is not found, or if one has lost teeth or has a mouth condition. For women, chewing gum is a substitute.
The key is the intention to clean the teeth.
2
Understand the evidence for substitutes
The hadith 'The fingers suffice for siwak' and the saying of Ali that rubbing with index finger and thumb is siwak provide the proof.
These are ahadith, so they establish the ruling.
3
Learn the proper method of holding
The sunnah is to hold the siwak with the right hand: little finger below, ring and index above, thumb below the head. Avoid gripping with the full fist, as it causes hemorrhoids.
This is based on a narration of Ibn Mas'ud.
4
Apply the ruling to modern contexts
Today, a toothbrush or even a finger can serve as a substitute if a miswak is not available. The ruling teaches flexibility while maintaining the sunnah.
The underlying goal is oral hygiene and seeking reward.

في ابتدائه، ولو بالإصْبَع عند فَقْدِهِ. أو « مَعَ كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ » ). ولما ورد « أنَّ كُلَّ صَلَاةٍ بِهِ تفضلُ سَبْعِينَ صَلاة بدونـه » . وينبغي أن يـكـون ليناً في غلط الإصبع، طول شبر مستوياً، قليل العقد من الأشجار المعروفة، وهي: الأراك، ليكون أقطع للبلغم، وأنقى للصدر، وأهني للطعام، وأن يستاك عرضاً، لا طولاً، لئلا يضـر لـحـم الأسـنان، وعليه الأكثر. وقال « الغزنوي » : يستاك طولاً وعرضاً ( في ابتدائـه)، أي الوضوء. ونص عليه، لأن الابتداء به سنة أيضاً. ووقته عند المضمضة على قول الأكثر. وقال غيرهم قبل الوضوء، والسواك من سنن الوضوء عندنا لا من سنن الصلاة، فيحصل فضيلته في كل صلاة صلاها بوضوء استاك فيـه مـن غير استياك عند قيامه لها. وليس السواك من خصائص الوضوء، فإنه يستحب في حالات، منها تغير الفم، والقيام من النوم، وإلى الصلاة، ودخول البيت واجتماع الناس، وقراءة القرآن والحديث، لقول أبي حنيفة: إن السواك من سنن الدين، فيستوي فيه الأحوال كلها. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: السَّوَاكُ مَطْهَرَةٌ لِلْفَمِ، مَرْضَاةٌ لِلرَّبِّ». وفضيلة السواك تحصل (وَلَو) كان الاستياك (بالإصبع)، أو خرقة خشنة (عند فقده)، أي: السواك أو فقد أسنانه، أو ضرر بفمه. لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: يُجْزِئُ مِنَ السَّوَاكِ الأصَابِعُ ). وقال علي : « التشويص) بالمسبحة والإبـهـام ســواك». ويقــوم العلك مقامه للنساء، لرقة بشرتهن ويستحب إمساكه باليد اليمني والسنة في كيفية أخذه، أن تجعل الخنصر من يمينك أسفل السواك، والبنصر والسبابة فوقه، واجعل الإبهام أسفل رأسه. كما رواه ابن مسعود ). ولا تقبض القبضة على السواك، فإنه يورث الباسور).

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the rulings of siwak. It begins by stating that siwak is recommended at the start of wudu, and even with a finger if no twig is available. It cites a hadith that prayer with siwak is 70 times better. The preferred siwak is from arak, soft, a span long, straight, few knots. It should be used widthwise to avoid gum harm. Al-Ghaznawi added that it should be used both lengthwise and widthwise at the start of wudu. The time for siwak according to most scholars is during mouth rinsing (madmadah), others say before wudu. Importantly, in the Hanafi school, siwak is a sunnah of wudu, not of prayer. This means its virtue is achieved as long as one used siwak during wudu, even if not repeated for the prayer. Siwak is not restricted to wudu; it is recommended in many situations. Abu Hanifa considered it a sunnah of the religion, applicable in all states. The hadith 'siwak purifies the mouth' is cited. Even if one cannot use a twig, using a finger or rough cloth attains the virtue. For women, gum chewing is a substitute. The proper method of holding is described: little finger below, ring and index above, thumb below the head. Grip should not be a full fist as it causes hemorrhoids.

Key Terms
التشويص (al-tashwīṣ): Rubbing the teeth with the finger, as a substitute for siwak.
العلك (al-‘ilk): Chewing gum, used as a substitute for siwak for women due to delicate skin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the recommended substitute for siwak for women?
A) A rough cloth.
B) Chewing gum.
C) The finger only.
D) No substitute; they must use a miswak.

Key Takeaway
The virtue of siwak is attained even with substitutes like finger or cloth; women may use chewing gum, and the proper grip method is part of the sunnah.

Definitions and Sunnah Practice of Madmadah and Istinshaq
Defining madmadah and istinshaq and their sunnah practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of madmadah and istinshaq, apply the sunnah method (three times with fresh water), and identify the ruling when using one scoop.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah muakkadah in wudu; using one scoop for three rinses still fulfills the sunnah but with lesser virtue.

In this passage, the author defines the acts of rinsing the mouth and sniffing water in wudu, and clarifies their sunnah nature. The text emphasizes that the optimal practice is to use fresh water for each of the three repetitions, but a single scoop still suffices for the basic sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Identify the two acts: madmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water). Note their linguistic and technical definitions.
2
Determine the sunnah method
From the text, state the number of repetitions and the requirement for water: three times, each with fresh water.
3
Analyze the exception
Examine the case where one uses a single scoop for all three rinses. What ruling does the text give?
The text says the sunnah of madmadah is fulfilled, but the sunnah of separate scoops is missed.
4
Compare virtue
Understand the difference between fulfilling the sunnah and achieving the full reward.
Using separate scoops is superior in virtue.

Source Text

والمَضْمَضَةُ)، وهي اصطلاحاً: استيعاب الماء جميع الفم. وفي اللغة: التحريك. وأن تكـــون (ثلاثاً)؛ لأنه تَوَضَّأَ فَمَضْمَضَ ثَلاثاً، واسْتَنْشَقَ ثَلاثَاً، يَأخُذُ بِكُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مَاءً جَدِيدَاً (۳)، (ولو) تمضمض ثلاثاً (بغَرْفَةٍ)، كان مقيماً لسنة المضمضة، لا سنّة تكرير الغرفات، فيكون دون الأول في الفضل. والاسْتِنْشَاقُ)، وهو لغة من النشق وهو : جذب الماء ونحوه بريح الأنف إلى داخله.

Commentary
This passage defines the terms madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water into the nose) and explains their performance as sunnah acts of wudu. Madmadah technically means moving water throughout the mouth, and linguistically just movement. The sunnah is to do each three times, each time with fresh water, as the Prophet did. However, even if one uses a single scoop of water for all three rinses, the sunnah of madmadah is still fulfilled (though the sunnah of separate scoops is missed), resulting in a lesser reward. Istinshaq is defined linguistically as drawing water into the nose. Both are sunnah acts in wudu according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المضمضة (al-madmaḍah): The act of rinsing the mouth by circulating water throughout the mouth. Technically: complete circulation; linguistically: movement.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshāq): Drawing water into the nose and sniffing it back.

Ruling on Siwak While Lying Down
States the ruling and its reason, then expands on benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using siwak while lying down and explain the reason for the dislike.

Core Idea
Using siwak while lying down is disliked because it may cause enlargement of the spleen.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the posture during the recommended act of using the siwak (miswak). While the siwak itself is a highly emphasized sunnah, the manner of its use can affect its legal desirability. The text states that using it while lying down is makruh (disliked), and it provides a health-based reason. Understanding this distinction helps us apply fiqh principles to daily acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its base ruling
First, note that the siwak itself is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) in the Hanafi school. The act under discussion is using the siwak while lying down.
Base ruling of siwak is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Recognize the specific ruling
The text explicitly states 'yukrah' (it is disliked), so the ruling for the act in this posture is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked, not sinful).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid, but doing it is not sinful.
3
Understand the reason for dislike
The text gives a medical reason: it causes enlargement of the spleen (al-ṭiḥāl). This is a valid 'illa (cause) that triggers the ruling. The Hanafi school considers health harms as a basis for dislike.
The 'illa is not always explicitly given in fiqh texts, but here it is stated.
4
Differentiate from the general benefits
The passage then lists many benefits of siwak in a poem. These benefits do not remove the dislike of the specific posture; they emphasize the virtue of siwak in general.
The benefits are about the act itself, not about lying down.

The Sunan of Madmadah and Istinshaq in Wudu
Definition and proof of sunnah acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on madmadah and istinshaq, define them both technically, and explain the difference in performing them with one handful versus three handfuls.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah mu'akkadah; three separate handfuls are more virtuous, but madmadah can be done with one handful while istinshaq cannot.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah explains the sunnah acts of rinsing the mouth and sniffling water into the nose during wudu. The author defines both terms, states their ruling, and clarifies the method of performing them three times, highlighting a subtle difference between madmadah and istinshaq regarding the use of a single handful. Understanding these details ensures one performs wudu with the proper sunnah virtues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
Locate the statement that madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah. Recognise that they are sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) in the Hanafi school.
The passage states the acts are to be performed, implying sunnah.
2
Understand the definitions
Read the linguistic and terminological definitions: madmadah means moving water in the mouth to cover all parts; istinshaq means drawing water into the nose until it reaches the marin (soft part).
The author provides both language and technical meanings.
3
Analyse the proof
The hadith (from al-Tabarani) shows the Prophet performed them three times with fresh water. This is the basis for the sunnah.
The Hanafi principle: continuous practice of the Prophet without prohibition indicates sunnah, not fard.
4
Examine the method of three times
The sunnah is to do each three times, each time with a new handful (ghurfah). But the passage notes an exception: madmadah can be done with one handful used three times, though this is less virtuous.
For istinshaq, three times with one handful is not valid because the nose cannot hold the used water.
5
Apply to practice
In wudu, the most virtuous method is to take three separate handfuls for madmadah and three separate handfuls for istinshaq. If water is limited, madmadah can be done with one handful three times, but istinshaq still requires three handfuls.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and impacts daily wudu practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المضمضة ثلاثاً، ولو بغرفة، والاستنشاق. والمضمضة، وهي اصطلاحاً: استيعاب الماء جميع الفم. وفي اللغة: التحريك. وأن تكون (ثلاثاً)؛ لأنه توضأ فمضمض ثلاثاً، واستنشق ثلاثاً، يأخذ بكل واحدة ماءً جديداً (3)، (ولو) تمضمض ثلاثاً (بغرفة)، كان مقيماً لسنة المضمضة، لا سنة تكرير الغرفات، فيكون دون الأول في الفضل. والاستنشاق، وهو لغة من النشق وهو: جذب الماء ونحوه بريح الأنف إلى داخله. واصطلاحاً: أن يصل الماء إلى المارن، وهو ما لان من الأنف، ويكون ( بثلاث غرفات)، لما تقدم، وقيد بثلاث غرفات؛ لأنه لا يصح التثليث بغرفة، لعدم انطباق الأنف على باقي الماء، بخلاف المضمضة. (3) أخرجه الطبراني في المعجم الكبير (180/19)، وذكره الزيلعي في نصب الراية (17/1).
Rinsing the mouth three times, even if with one handful, and sniffling water into the nose. And rinsing the mouth, terminologically: making water reach all parts of the mouth. Linguistically: moving (the water). And that it be three times; because he performed wudu and rinsed his mouth three times and sniffled three times, taking new water for each. And if he rinses three times with one handful, he has fulfilled the sunnah of rinsing, not the sunnah of repeating handfuls, so it is lesser in virtue. And sniffing water into the nose, linguistically from 'nasq' meaning drawing water etc. with the breath of the nose inwardly. Terminologically: that water reaches the marin (the soft part of the nose), and it is with three handfuls, due to what preceded. And it is restricted to three handfuls because three (times) is not valid with one handful, due to the inability of the nose to contain the remaining water, unlike rinsing.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, expanding on the base text. It defines the sunnah acts of madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffling water into the nose) in wudu. The author states that both are sunnah and are performed three times each, taking new water for each round. An important point: if one performs madmadah three times using a single handful of water (i.e., taking water, rinsing, then spitting back into the same water?), this fulfills the sunnah of madmadah but not the sunnah of using separate handfuls; hence it is less virtuous. For istinshaq, however, three times cannot be done with one handful because the nose cannot hold the used water; thus separate handfuls are required. The proof is the hadith that the Prophet performed wudu and did each three times, taking new water. This hadith is referenced from al-Tabarani. The definition of istinshaq: water must reach the marin (the soft part of the nose).

Key Terms
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water, making water reach all parts of the mouth.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshāq): Sniffling water into the nose until it reaches the soft part (marin).
الغرفة (al-ghurfah): A handful of water (the amount taken in the cupped hand).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The sunnah of madmadah is fulfilled but not the sunnah of repeating handfuls, so it is less virtuous.
C) It is valid but not recommended.
D) It is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah mu'akkadah in wudu; performing them three times with separate handfuls is more virtuous, but madmadah can be done with one handful while istinshaq requires separate handfuls.

Mubalaghah in Madmadah and Istinshaq for Non-Fasting Person
Ruling with proof on mubalaghah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mubalaghah in wudu for non-fasting persons, define the limits of mubalaghah, and apply the exception for fasting persons.

Core Idea
Exaggeration in rinsing and sniffling is sunnah for the non-fasting, but forbidden for the fasting to protect the fast.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies that while thoroughness in wudu is recommended, the degree of exaggeration in mouth rinsing and nasal sniffling depends on whether one is fasting. The Sunnah provides clear guidance: the command to exaggerate is coupled with an explicit exception for the fasting person. Understanding this nuance ensures proper wudu without compromising the fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is mubalaghah (exaggeration) in madmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (sniffling water) during wudu. The ruling for a non-fasting person is sunnah (recommended).
2
Understand the definitions
Mubalaghah in madmadah means making water reach the top of the throat. In istinshaq, it means making water reach above the marin (the soft part of the nose). These definitions set the limit of exaggeration.
3
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'أسْبِعْ الْوُضُوءَ ... وَبَالِغُ فِي الاسْتِنْشَاقِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ صَائِمًا' (Perform wudu thoroughly... and exaggerate in sniffling unless you are fasting). A second hadith from Ibn al-Qattan includes both madmadah and istinshaq.
Hadith from the four Sunan.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The imperative 'بالغ' indicates obligation in principle, but the exception 'إلا أن تكون صائمًا' provides a qarīnah that it is not obligatory for all. Thus, it is sunnah (recommended) for the non-fasting.
Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub illa li qarinah.
5
Note the practical application
Fasting persons must avoid exaggeration to prevent water from entering the throat or stomach, which could invalidate the fast. They should perform madmadah and istinshaq without reaching the extreme limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يُسنُ المُبَالَغَةُ في المَضْمَضَةِ)، وهي أن يصل الماء رأس الحلق. (و) المبالغة في الاسْتِنْشَاقِ) وهي: إيصال الماء إلى ما فوق المارن (لَغَيْر الصَّائم)، والصائم لا يبالغ فيهما خشية إلحاق الفساد بالصوم، لقوله : ( أسْبِعْ الْوُضُوءَ وَخَلَّلْ بَيْنَ الأَصَابِعِ وَبَالِغُ فِي الاسْتِنْشَاقِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ صَائِمًا » (۳). رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة. وروى ابن القطان بسند صحيح: « وَبَالِغ في المَضْمَضَةِ وَالاسْتِنْشَاق (۳). (3) ذكره الزيلعي في نصب الراية (16/1) وقال: ذكره ابن القطان في كتابه الوهم والإيهام.
And it is sunnah to exaggerate in rinsing the mouth, which is making water reach the top of the throat. And exaggeration in sniffling water is making water reach above the marin (soft part of the nose), for a non-fasting person. The fasting person does not exaggerate in them out of fear of spoiling the fast, because of his saying: 'Perform wudu thoroughly, and comb between the fingers, and exaggerate in sniffling unless you are fasting.' Related by the authors of the four Sunan. And Ibn al-Qattan related with a sound chain: 'And exaggerate in rinsing the mouth and sniffling.'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that it is sunnah (recommended) to exaggerate (mubalaghah) in madmadah and istinshaq for a person who is not fasting. For madmadah, exaggeration means making water reach as far as the top of the throat. For istinshaq, it means making water reach above the marin (the soft part of the nose). However, a fasting person should not exaggerate in these acts because it might cause water to enter the throat or stomach, thus breaking the fast. The proof is a hadith from the four Sunan: '...and exaggerate in sniffling unless you are fasting.' Another hadith from Ibn al-Qattan includes both madmadah and istinshaq. The Hanafi school uses these hadith to establish the sunnah nature of mubalaghah for non-fasting individuals.

Key Terms
المبالغة (al-mubālaghah): Exaggeration or thoroughness; in madmadah: reaching the throat; in istinshaq: reaching above the marin.
المارن (al-mārin): The soft part of the nose (the fleshy tip).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Should a fasting person exaggerate in sniffling water during wudu?
A) Yes, it is sunnah
B) No, they should avoid exaggeration
C) It is wajib
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Mubalaghah in madmadah and istinshaq is sunnah for non-fasting persons, but avoided by fasting persons to protect the fast.

Sunnah of Combing the Beard in Wudu: The Internal Hanafi Dispute
Presents the ruling and internal Hanafi dispute on combing the beard during wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the internal Hanafi dispute regarding combing the beard during wudu, identify the evidence used by each side, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Combing the beard in wudu is sunnah in the preferred Hanafi view, despite disagreement among the founding imams.

In this lesson, we examine an internal Hanafi dispute about the status of combing the beard (takhleel al-lihyah) during wudu. While Abu Yusuf considers it a sunnah act, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani do not. By understanding the reasoning of each imam and the tarjih (preferment) that settled the matter, you will gain insight into how Hanafi scholars resolve disagreements within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act and the Hanafi imams involved
The act is combing the thick beard after washing the face three times. The imams are Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
State the position of Abu Yusuf and his evidence
Abu Yusuf holds it is sunnah. His evidence is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet combed his beard and said 'My Lord commanded me to do this.'
3
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad and their evidence
They hold it is not sunnah. Their evidence: lack of constancy (muwazabah) of the Prophet's action, and the principle that sunnah completes the fard, but the inside of the beard is not part of the face for fard washing.
4
Analyse the tarjih and why Abu Yusuf's view is preferred
Al-Mabsut (al-Sarakhsi) prefers Abu Yusuf's view because the explicit hadith outweighs the qiyas-based argument. The text says 'fi al-ashah' (most correct) is sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Following Abu Yusuf, omitting combing means missing a sunnah; following Abu Hanifa, no sunnah is missed. In practice, most Hanafis follow Abu Yusuf as the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن في الأصح تَخْلِيلُ اللحية الكثة)، وهو قول أبي يوسف. لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يُخَللُ لِحْيَتَهُ » . والتخليل تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق، ويـكـون بـعـد غسل الوجه ثلاثاً، بِكَفِّ مَاءٍ مِنْ أسْفَلِهَا)، لرواية أبي داود عن أنس : «كَانَ النبي ، إِذا تَوَضًا أحَدٌ كَفَّاً مِنْ مَاء تحتَ حَنَكِهِ فخلَّلَ به لحيتَهُ»، وقال: ( بِهَذَا أَمَرَنِي رَبِّي )، وأبو حنيفة ومحمد يفضلان تخليل اللحية لعدم ثبوت المواظبة، ولكون السنة لإكمال الفرض في محله، وداخلها ليس بمحل لإقامته، فلا يكون التخليل إكمالاً، فلا يكون سنة، بخلاف الأصابع، ورجح في « المبسوط » قول أبي يوسف الرواية أنس له. (4) أخرجه الترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في تخليل اللحية (31) ، وابن ماجه في الطهارة وسننها، باب: مــا جـاء في تخليل اللحية (430). (5) أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب تخليل اللحية (145)، والطبراني في المعجم الأوسط (221/3). (6) أي: السنة، وذكر باعتبار أنها مأمور به. ط.
And it is sunnah, according to the most correct view, to comb the thick beard, and this is the saying of Abu Yusuf. Because the Prophet used to comb his beard. And combing means separating the hair from below upward, and it is done after washing the face three times, with a handful of water from underneath it (the chin), due to the narration of Abu Dawud from Anas: 'The Prophet, when he performed wudu, would take a handful of water under his chin and comb his beard with it,' and he said, 'My Lord commanded me to do this.' Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prefer the view that combing the beard is not sunnah, due to lack of confirmed constancy, and because the sunnah is to complete the obligatory washing in its place, and the inside of the beard is not a place for performing it, so combing is not completion, hence not sunnah, unlike the fingers. And in al-Mabsut, the view of Abu Yusuf is preferred due to the hadith of Anas.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is whether combing (takhleel) the beard during wudu is sunnah. The commentator states that the most correct view (al-ashah) is that it is sunnah, which is the position of Abu Yusuf. The evidence is that the Prophet used to comb his beard, as narrated by Anas. The method is to take a handful of water from under the chin and comb the beard upward after washing the face three times. However, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that it is not sunnah. Their reasoning: the sunnah is meant to complete the obligatory (fard) washing of the face, but the inside of the beard is not considered part of the face for wudu (since the face is washed externally), so combing does not complete the fard. Therefore, it is not sunnah. They also argue that the Prophet's action was not constant (muwazabah) enough to establish sunnah. Despite this, the author of al-Mabsut (al-Sarakhsi) preferred Abu Yusuf's view due to the explicit hadith. In practice, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that combing the beard is sunnah, as stated here (fi al-ashah).

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (takhleel al-lihyah): Combing or separating the hair of the beard with wet fingers, typically from below upward, during wudu.
الكثة (al-kaththah): Thick, dense (beard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) All of them

Key Takeaway
The most correct Hanafi view is that combing the beard during wudu is a sunnah act, based on the hadith of Anas, even though there was internal disagreement among the early imams.

Sunnah of Combing the Fingers in Wudu
States the unanimous sunnah of combing fingers and toes during wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (sunnah) on combing fingers and toes during wudu, cite the hadith proof, and explain why it is sunnah and not fard in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Combing fingers and toes is sunnah by consensus; the command indicates recommendation, not obligation.

In this lesson, we examine a short but important sunnah of wudu: combing (takhleel) the fingers of the hands and feet. The text from Nur al-Idah states that this is sunnah by agreement (bil-ittifaq), supported by a prophetic hadith. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and why it is classified as sunnah rather than fard, using Hanafi usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states: '(و) يسن (تَخْلِيلُ الأصابع كلها من اليدين والرجلين)' – 'And it is sunnah to comb all the fingers of both hands and feet.' So the act is takhleel, and the ruling is sunnah.
Sunnah here is in the fiqh sense: recommended, not obligatory.
2
Note the consensus indicator
The phrase 'بالاتفاق' (by agreement) indicates that the three imams of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) are unanimous on this. In fact, other schools also consider it sunnah.
This unanimity is important for fatwa.
3
Examine the first proof: hadith with command
The text cites the hadith: 'إِذَا تَوَضاتَ، فَخَلَّل أصابعَ يَدَيْكَ ورجليك' (When you perform wudu, comb between your fingers of hands and feet). The imperative 'khalil' normally indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul, but here it is interpreted as sunnah due to other evidence (e.g., no penalty for leaving it).
This is a key usul principle: the command can be downgraded from fard to sunnah if there is evidence of non-obligation.
4
Consider the second (cut-off) proof
The text begins a second hadith: 'مَنْ لَمْ يُخَلل' (Whoever does not comb...). Though cut off, it likely implies a milder consequence. This further supports the recommended nature.
The full hadith is not needed to establish the sunnah ruling.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul: command downgraded to sunnah
Hanafi scholars ruled that takhleel is sunnah because: (a) the command is not accompanied by a penalty for omission, (b) there is no Quranic verse making it obligatory, (c) the practice of the Prophet was consistent but not emphasized as fard.
This demonstrates how usul al-fiqh shapes fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (تَخْلِيلُ الأصابع كلها من اليدين والرجلين، بالاتفاق لما تقدم، ولقوله : ( إِذَا تَوَضاتَ، فَخَلَّل أصابعَ يَدَيْكَ ورجليك . ولقوله : « مَنْ لَمْ يُخَلل (٤) (7) أخرجه الترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في تخليل الأصابع (39) ، وابن ماجه في كتاب الطهارة، باب: تخليل الأصابع (447)، والزيلعي في نصب الراية (27/1).
And it is sunnah to comb all the fingers of the hands and feet, by agreement, due to what preceded, and due to his saying: 'When you perform wudu, comb between your fingers of hands and feet.' And due to his saying: 'Whoever does not comb...'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that combing (takhleel) the fingers of both hands and feet is sunnah in wudu, and there is consensus (bil-ittifaq) on this among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The proof includes a hadith commanding the combing of fingers. Another hadith begins but is cut off in the text. The footnote provides sources from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah. This sunnah is established by the explicit command of the Prophet and the practice. Unlike the beard combing, there was no dispute on finger combing because it directly aids in the washing of the fingers, which are part of the limbs to be washed.

Key Terms
تخليل الأصابع (takhleel al-asābi'): Combing or interlocking the fingers and toes with water during wudu to ensure water reaches between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Makruh
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Combing fingers and toes is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in wudu, supported by a hadith and consensus, but not obligatory.

Sunnah of Thorough Rinsing and Snuffing in Wudu
Explanation of sunnah mubalaghah with definition, ruling, and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of mubalaghah in madhmadah and istinshaq, define mubalaghah terminologically, and identify the hadith evidence with its specific exception for fasting.

Core Idea
Mubalaghah in mouth and nose rinsing is sunnah mu'akkadah for non-fasting persons, prohibited for fasting persons to avoid breaking the fast.

In this lesson, we examine the sunnah of thorough rinsing (mubalaghah) during wudu. The source defines what mubalaghah means in the mouth and nose, and provides the prophetic instruction that clarifies when it applies — with a crucial exception for the fasting person. Understanding this nuance prevents violating the fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is mubalaghah in madhmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (snuffing water into nose). The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah for a non-fasting person.
The act is not fard or wajib, but a highly recommended sunnah.
2
Define mubalaghah technically
For madhmadah, mubalaghah means water reaches the root of the throat. For istinshaq, it means water reaches above the soft part of the nose (marin).
The definition distinguishes between the two actions.
3
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Perform wudu thoroughly, and do khilaal between fingers, and do mubalaghah in snuffing unless you are fasting.' (Narrated by the four Sunan). A second hadith (Ibn al-Qattan) includes madhmadah as well.
Both hadith are ahad (single-narrator), but accepted for sunnah rulings.
4
Interpret the dalil
The imperative 'baligh' indicates a sunnah (not fard) in Hanafi usul. The exception 'illa an takuna sa'iman' explicitly removes the ruling for a fasting person.
The exception proves that mubalaghah is not intended for fasting persons.
5
Apply the exception
For a fasting person, performing mubalaghah is makruh (disliked) because it risks water entering and breaking the fast. Such a person should rinse gently.
This preserves the validity of the fast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بثلاثِ غَرَفَاتِ، والمبالغة في المضمضة والاستنشاق لغير الصائم، وتخليلُ اللحية الكثة بكف ماء من أسفلها، وتخليلُ الأصابع. واصطلاحاً: أن يصل الماء إلى المارن، وهو ما لان من الأنف، ويكون ( بثلاثِ عَرَفَاتِ)، لما تقدم)، وقيد بثلاث غرفات؛ لأنه لا يصح التثليث بغرفة، لعدم انطباق الأنف عـلـى بـاقـي المـاء، بخلاف المضمضة. (وَ) يُسنُ المُبَالَغَةُ في المَضْمَضَةِ)، وهي أن يصل الماء رأس الحلق. (و) المبالغة في الاسْتِنْشَاقِ) وهي: إيصال الماء إلى ما فوق المارن (لَغَيْر الصَّائم)، والصائم لا يبالغ فيهما خشية إلحاق الفساد بالصوم، لقوله : ( أسْبِعْ الْوُضُوءَ وَخَلَّلْ بَيْنَ الأَصَابِعِ وَبَالِغُ فِي الاسْتِنْشَاقِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ صَائِمًا » (۳). رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة. وروى ابن القطان بسند صحيح: « وَبَالِغ في المَضْمَضَةِ وَالاسْتِنْشَاق (۳).
With three handfuls, and mubalaghah in rinsing mouth and snuffing for non-fasting person, and khilaal of thick beard with a palm of water from below it, and khilaal of fingers. Terminologically: that water reaches the marin, which is the soft part of nose, and it is with three handfuls, due to what preceded, and restricted to three handfuls because triple action with one handful is not valid, because the nose does not cover the rest of water, unlike rinsing mouth. And it is sunnah to do mubalaghah in rinsing mouth, which is to make water reach the head of the throat. And mubalaghah in snuffing, which is to make water reach above the marin, for non-fasting person. And the fasting person does not do mubalaghah in these two for fear of spoiling the fast, due to his saying sallallahu alayhi wa sallam: 'Perform wudu thoroughly, and khilaal between fingers, and do mubalaghah in snuffing unless you are fasting' - narrated by the four Sunan. And Ibn al-Qattan narrated with a sound chain: 'And do mubalaghah in rinsing mouth and snuffing.'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the sunnah acts of wudu, specifically mubalaghah (thoroughness) in madhmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (snuffing water into nose). The author defines mubalaghah: for the mouth, it means water reaches the root of the throat; for the nose, it means water reaches above the soft part (marin). The matn specifies that this is for non-fasting persons only; a fasting person should not go to extremes because water might enter the throat or stomach and break the fast. The proof is the hadith commanding mubalaghah except when fasting, narrated by the authors of the Sunan. Additionally, the hadith of Ibn al-Qattan includes both rinsing and snuffing. The passage also explains that the triple sprinkling (tathleeth) for istinshaq is with three separate handfuls, unlike for madhmadah where one handful suffices for three rinses, because the nose cannot cover the water from one handful.

Key Terms
مبالغة (mubālaghah): Thoroughness in rinsing mouth and snuffing water into nose to the maximum without causing harm.
مارن (mārin): The soft part of the nose above which water should reach for mubalaghah in istinshaq.

Khilaal of the Beard: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sunnah Status
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khilaal of beard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on khilaal of the beard and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Khilaal of the beard is sunnah according to the preferred view, though Imams differed on its constancy.

In this passage, we examine an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Is khilaal (passing water through) a thick beard a sunnah act in wudu? Abu Yusuf holds it is sunnah, citing explicit prophetic practice, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it merely recommended. Our lesson unpacks the evidence and the tarjih that settles the school's operative position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
The act in question is khilaal of a thick beard (takhlīl al-liḥyah al-kaththah) during wudu. Determine the legal nature of this act: is it sunnah, mustahabb, or something else?
The dispute is about its status, not its permissibility.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and dalil
Abu Yusuf argues that it is sunnah, based on the hadith of Anas (ra) in which the Prophet (saw) performed khilaal and stated 'My Lord commanded me with this.' Identify the source and the implication.
The hadith is recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
State Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it is not sunnah but merely preferable (mustahabb). Their reasoning: lack of confirmed constancy (muwāẓabah) by the Prophet, and because the interior of the beard is not the place of the fard (washing the face), so khilaal does not complete the obligation.
They compare this to khilaal of fingers, which is sunnah because fingers are part of the hand.
4
Examine the tarjih mechanism
Al-Mabsut (by al-Sarakhsi) weighs the evidence and prefers Abu Yusuf's view due to the explicit hadith. Understand why this view becomes the mufta bihi.
The tarjih authority is al-Mabsut, a foundational text of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن في الأصح تَخْلِيلُ اللحية الكثة)، وهو قول أبي يوسف. لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يُخَللُ لِحْيَتَهُ » . والتخليل تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق، ويـكـون بـعـد غسل الوجه ثلاثاً، بِكَفِّ مَاءٍ مِنْ أسْفَلِهَا)، لرواية أبي داود عن أنس : «كَانَ النبي ، إِذا تَوَضًا أحَدٌ كَفَّاً مِنْ مَاء تحتَ حَنَكِهِ فخلَّلَ به لحيتَهُ»، وقال: ( بِهَذَا أَمَرَنِي رَبِّي )، وأبو حنيفة ومحمد يفضلان تخليل اللحية لعدم ثبوت المواظبة، ولكون السنة لإكمال الفرض في محله، وداخلها ليس بمحل لإقامته، فلا يكون التخليل إكمالاً، فلا يكون سنة، بخلاف الأصابع، ورجح في « المبسوط » قول أبي يوسف الرواية أنس له.
And it is sunnah according to the soundest view to do khilaal of the thick beard, and that is the statement of Abu Yusuf, because the Prophet sallallahu alayhi wa sallam used to do khilaal of his beard. Al-takhleel is to part the hair from below upwards, and it is done after washing the face three times, with a palm of water from its underside, due to the narration of Abu Dawud from Anas: 'The Prophet, when he performed wudu, would take a palm of water under his jaw and do khilaal of his beard with it,' and he said: 'My Lord commanded me with this.' And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider khilaal of beard as preferable (but not sunnah) due to lack of confirmed constancy, and because the sunnah is to complete the obligatory act in its place, and what is inside the beard is not a place for fulfilling the obligation, so khilaal is not a completion, thus not sunnah, unlike fingers. And in al-Mabsut, the view of Abu Yusuf is preferred due to the narration of Anas.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of khilaal (passing water through) of a thick beard. The soundest view (al-ashahh) is that it is sunnah, which is the position of Abu Yusuf. His evidence is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet used to do khilaal of his beard and said it was commanded by his Lord. The method is to take a palm of water from below the beard and part the hair upward after washing the face three times. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it is not sunnah because the Prophet's constancy is not established, and the beard's interior is not part of the face to be washed, so khilaal does not complete the obligation. They argue that sunnah is what completes the fard in its place, and since the beard's interior is not the place of the fard (which is the skin of the face), khilaal is not a completion. However, al-Mabsut prefers Abu Yusuf's view due to the explicit narration. Thus, the mufta bihi (operative position) in the school is that it is sunnah.

Key Terms
تخليل (takhlīl): Passing water through the beard by parting the hair from below upwards.
الكثة (al-kaththah): Thick beard that conceals the skin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Khilaal of a thick beard is a sunnah act in wudu according to the mufta bihi of the Hanafi school, based on the hadith of Anas and the tarjih of al-Mabsut.

Sunnah of Khilaal of Fingers in Wudu
Ruling on khilaal of fingers with unanimous agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khilaal of fingers in wudu (sunnah, not wajib) and explain the evidence and the method.

Core Idea
Khilaal of fingers is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib — the command was diverted by context.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on passing water between the fingers and toes during wudu. The text confirms it is unanimously sunnah and provides the evidence and method. We will understand why it is not wajib despite the imperative form, and how the method is not strictly prescribed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that khilaal of all fingers (hands and feet) is sunnah, by agreement of the scholars. This is the ruling on this act.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith: 'When you perform wudu, do khilaal of your fingers and toes.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) is cited as evidence. The imperative form indicates a command, but the ruling is still sunnah.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which affects the level of obligation.
3
Understand why it is not wajib
Despite the imperative, there is a diverting factor (sarf): the command was given in the context of teaching a Bedouin, and the Prophet's own practice sometimes omitted khilaal. Therefore, it is not obligatory.
The absence of khilaal in narrated descriptions of the Prophet's wudu supports this.
4
Note the corroborating hadith
Another hadith threatens punishment for omitting khilaal, which underscores its importance but does not change the ruling from sunnah to wajib because the evidence for obligation is overridden.
5
Analyze the method's binding nature
Al-Kamal notes that the exact method (interlacing for hands, little finger for feet) is not a specific sunnah but rather incidental. Thus, any method that achieves passing water between fingers suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (تَخْلِيلُ الأصابع كلها من اليدين والرجلين، بالاتفاق لما تقدم، ولقوله : ( إِذَا تَوَضاتَ، فَخَلَّل أصابعَ يَدَيْكَ ورجليك . ولقوله : « مَنْ لَمْ يُخَلل أصابعه بالماء، خللها الله بالنارِ يومَ القيامةِ » (). ولم يكن واجباً بالأمر في قوله : ( أمرني ربي » (٢). وخللوا لوجود الصارف، وهو تعليم الأعرابي)، وعدم ذكر التخليل فيمـا حـكـي مـن وضوئه . وكيفية تخليل أصابع اليدين أن يدخل بعضها في بعض، ويقوم مقامه الإدخال في الماء الجاري، وما هو في حكمه. وصفته في الرجلين أن يخلل بخنصر يده اليسرى خنصـر رجـلـه الـيـمنـي ابتداء، ويختم بخنصر رجله اليسرى. كذا ورد). قال « الكمال » : والله أعلم أنه أمر اتفاقي، لا سنة مقصودة، فلا تختص سنة التخليل بهذه الكيفية.
And it is sunnah to do khilaal of all fingers of hands and feet, by agreement due to what preceded, and due to his saying sallallahu alayhi wa sallam: 'When you perform wudu, do khilaal of your fingers and toes.' And due to his saying: 'Whoever does not do khilaal of his fingers with water, Allah will do khilaal of them with fire on the Day of Resurrection.' And it was not obligatory despite the command in his saying 'My Lord commanded me' because of the presence of a diverting factor, namely teaching the Bedouin, and the omission of khilaal in what has been narrated of his wudu. The method of khilaal for the hands is to interlace the fingers of one hand with the other, and putting them in running water or similar suffices. The description for the feet is to do khilaal with the little finger of the left hand starting with the little toe of the right foot and ending with the little toe of the left foot. Thus it is narrated. Al-Kamal said: Allah knows best that it is an incidental matter, not a specific sunnah, so the sunnah of khilaal is not restricted to this method.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on khilaal of all fingers (both hands and feet) during wudu. It is unanimously sunnah. The evidence includes hadiths commanding khilaal and threatening those who omit it. Despite the imperative form, khilaal is not wajib because the command was in a specific context (teaching the Bedouin) and the Prophet's own practice sometimes omitted it. The method for hands is to interlace fingers; for feet, it is to start with the little toe of the right foot using the left little finger and end with the left little toe. However, al-Kamal notes that this exact method is not a required sunnah; it is just how it was done incidentally.

Key Terms
تخليل الأصابع (takhlīl al-aṣābiʿ): Passing water between fingers by interlacing or inserting them in water.
صارف (ṣārif): A diverting factor that prevents a command from indicating obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is khilaal of fingers not obligatory despite the command in hadith?
A) The command was abrogated
B) The command was specific to teaching the Bedouin and the Prophet omitted it sometimes
C) It is fard kifayah
D) It is only for imams

Key Takeaway
Khilaal of fingers in wudu is a highly emphasised sunnah, not an obligation, and the method described is flexible.

The Sunnah of Triple Washing in Wudu and the Prohibition of Exceeding
Ruling on triple washing with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on triple washing in wudu, explain the prohibition on exceeding three, and identify the conditions under which extra washing is permissible.

Core Idea
Washing each limb three times is sunnah; adding more with the belief it is sunnah is blameworthy.

This lesson examines the sunnah of tathleeth—washing each wudu limb three times. We will study the evidence from the Prophet's demonstration and his statement that adding or subtracting from this practice is blameworthy. The commentary clarifies the contexts in which doing more than three is permissible, such as when renewing wudu or removing doubt.

Guided Path
1
State the sunnah of triple washing
Identify that washing each limb three times is a sunnah muakkadah, but note that this applies to washing, not wiping.
The restriction to ghsl (washing) is explicit in the text.
2
Analyze the hadith evidence
Read the hadith of the man who asked about purification. The Prophet demonstrated wudu by washing each limb three times, then said: 'This is wudu. Whoever adds to this or reduces, has done evil and wronged.'
The hadith is from Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah.
3
Interpret 'asa'a and zulm
Understand that 'asa'a (doing evil) refers to adding more than three, and zulm (wronging) refers to reducing, but only if the person believes the added/reduced number is part of the sunnah.
If one adds for a reason other than belief, it is not blameworthy.
4
Identify permissible reasons for extra washing
List scenarios where washing more than three times is permissible: intention of wudu upon wudu (renewal), to remove doubt about having washed properly, or due to scarcity of water.
These are exceptions to the general prohibition.
5
Distinguish washing from wiping
Note that repeating wiping of the head three times is not sunnah, unlike washing. The text restricts the sunnah of triple to washing alone.
This is because wiping is not subject to the same practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن (تَثْلِيتُ الغَسل)، قيد به لإفادة أنه لا يســن تكــرار المسح، لأن رجلاً أتى النبي ، فقال : « يا رسول الله، كيف الطهور؟ فدعا بماءٍ في إناء، فغسل كفيـهِ ثلاثاً، ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثاً، ثم غسل ذراعيه ثلاثاً، ثم مسح برأسه، ثم أدخل إصبعيه السباحتين في أذنيه، ومسح بإبهاميه على ظاهر أذنيه وبالسباحتينِ باطنُ أذنيه، ثم غسل رجليه ثلاثاً ثلاثاً ثم قال: هكذا الوضوء، فمن زاد على هذا أو نقص، فقد أساء وظلم»، وفي لفظ لابن ماجه « تـعــدى وظلم». والنسائي « أساء وتعدى وظلم ) ( ) أي : إذا اعتقد أن ذلك سنة، والإساءة بالزيادة، والظلم بالنقص. أما لو زاد لقصد الوضوء على الوضوء، أو لطمأنينة القلب عند الشك أو لنقص الحاجة لا بأس به.
And it is sunnah to wash three times (tathleeth al-ghusl), restricted to indicate that repeating wiping is not sunnah, because a man came to the Prophet sallallahu alayhi wa sallam and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, how is purification?' So he called for water in a vessel, and washed his hands three times, then washed his face three times, then washed his arms three times, then wiped his head, then inserted his two index fingers into his ears and wiped with his thumbs the outside of his ears and with his index fingers the inside of his ears, then washed his feet three times, then said: 'This is wudu. Whoever adds to this or reduces, has done evil and wronged.' In the wording of Ibn Majah: 'has transgressed and wronged.' And in al-Nasa'i: 'has done evil, transgressed and wronged.' That is, if he believes that to be sunnah. Doing evil applies to increase, and wrong applies to decrease. As for if he increases intending wudu upon wudu, or for reassurance of heart due to doubt, or for need of less water, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of triple washing (tathleeth) for wudu limbs. It is sunnah to wash each limb three times, but not to repeat wiping of the head three times. The evidence is the hadith where the Prophet demonstrated wudu washing each limb three times and then said that adding to or subtracting from this is blameworthy. The terms 'asa'a (did evil) and 'zalam (wronged) are interpreted: increasing in number (beyond three) is 'asa'a, decreasing (less than three) is zulm, but only if one believes that the extra or reduced number is sunnah. However, if one increases with the intention of performing wudu upon wudu (i.e., renewing wudu) or for certitude due to doubt, or due to lack of water (e.g., only have enough for one wash), then it is permissible. This is similar to hadith: the essential is to do three times, but deviation with ignorance of sunnah is not sinful.

Key Terms
تثليث (tathlīth): Washing each limb of wudu three times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible
B) He has done evil (asa'a)
C) It becomes wajib
D) Wudu is invalid

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to wash each limb three times; adding more with the belief that it is part of the sunnah is blameworthy, but permissible for other valid reasons.

Sunnah of Comprehensive Wiping of Head Once
Ruling that wiping entire head once is sunnah, not three times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that wiping the entire head once is sunnah, identify the hadith proof, and explain why triple wiping is not the sunnah.

Core Idea
The Prophet wiped his head once comprehensively – that is the sunnah, not three times.

In wudu, wiping the head is a fard, but the manner of wiping has a sunnah. Some people think wiping three times brings more reward. This passage clarifies that the sunnah is to wipe the entire head once, based on direct prophetic practice, and any reports of triple wiping are understood differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah act
Find the act being ruled as sunnah: comprehensive wiping of the head (isti'ab al-ra's) once during wudu.
Comprehensive means covering the entire head including front, back, temples, and ears.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The hadith of Rubayyi' bint Mu'awwidh states the Prophet wiped his head once. This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is recorded in Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the phrase 'once'
The explicit wording 'once' (marra wahida) indicates the sunnah is a single comprehensive wipe.
The author emphasizes that the word 'once' restricts the number.
4
Interpret triple wiping reports
Reports of triple wiping are explained as either to ensure full coverage or due to insufficient moisture, not as a regular practice.
The Prophet's practice was on ease (takhfif), unlike rinsing mouth and nose which require thoroughness.
5
Compare with other acts
Wiping once is likened to tayammum and wiping over a bandage (jabirah) where once suffices.
Rinsing mouth (madmadah) and snuffing (istinshaq) are different because they require three times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن ( اسْتِيعَابُ الرَّأْسِ بالمَسْحِ)، لما حكت الربيع بنت مسعود « أنها رأت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يتوضأ قالت: فمسح رأسه، ما أقبل منه، وما أدبر وصدغيه وأذنيه مرة واحدة . فلذا قيد المسح بقوله (مَرّةً)، ولتضافر الطرق الصحيحة على مسحه مرة واحدة؛ لإلحاقه بالتيمم والجبيرة ). وحمــل مـا ورد من تثليثه على تحقيق الاستيعاب، وحمل تعدد الماء فيه على قلة البلة، أو نفادها، لا ليكون سنة مستمرة، إذ وضعه على التخفيف بخلاف المضمضة والاستنشاق.
And it is sunnah to comprehensively wipe the head (isti'ab al-ra's bi al-mash), due to what Rubayyi' bint Mu'awwidh narrated: 'She saw the Prophet sallallahu alayhi wa sallam performing wudu, she said: He wiped his head, both front and back, and his temples and ears once.' Therefore he restricted the wiping by saying 'once', and due to the numerous authentic chains that he wiped once, to liken it to tayammum and jabirah (bandage). And what has been narrated of triple wiping is interpreted as achieving comprehensive coverage, and the multiplicity of water is interpreted as due to lack of moisture or its depletion, not as a continuous sunnah, because his practice was on ease, unlike rinsing mouth and snuffing.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage addresses the sunnah of wiping the entire head (isti'ab) once during wudu. The proof is the hadith of Rubayyi' bint Mu'awwidh that the Prophet wiped his head including front, back, temples, and ears only once. The author notes that despite some reports of triple wiping, they are interpreted as ensuring full coverage or due to insufficient water, not as a regular sunnah. Wiping three times is not sunnah; rather, it is sunnah to wipe once thoroughly. This is likened to tayammum and wiping over a bandage (jabirah) where once suffices. The rationale is that wudu is meant for ease, unlike madhmadah and istinshaq which require thoroughness.

Key Terms
استيعاب (istiʿāb): Covering the entire head with the wipe during masah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three times
B) Once
C) Twice
D) At least twice

Key Takeaway
Comprehensive wiping of the head once is the sunnah; triple wiping is not a sunnah but an interpretation of ensuring full coverage.

Sunnah of Tathlith and Isti'ab in Wudu
Establishes sunnah status and proofs of tathlith and isti'ab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of tathlith and isti'ab in wudu and cite the proof from the hadith of the Bedouin.

Core Idea
Tathlith and isti'ab are sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard, and overstepping this is blameworthy.

This lesson explains two important sunnah acts in wudu: washing each limb three times (tathlith) and wiping the entire head once (isti'ab). Understanding their status as sunnah rather than fard is crucial for correct practice. We will examine the primary proof from the hadith of the Bedouin and the Hanafi interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are the two acts described and what is their hukm level in the Hanafi school?
The passage states 'ويسن تثليث الغسل' and 'ويسن استيعاب الرأس بالمسح' indicating sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
What hadith does the author cite as the main evidence for tathlith and isti'ab?
The hadith of the Bedouin: the Prophet performed wudu three times and said 'هكذا الوضوء'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the Prophet's action and statement in the hadith prove the sunnah nature?
The action demonstrates the sunnah, and the statement 'فمن زاد على هذا أو نقص فقد أساء وظلم' shows that adding or reducing is blameworthy, implying the standard is sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
How does the Shafi'i school differ regarding wiping the head, and what is the Hanafi response?
Shafi'i considers wiping the entire head as fard; Hanafi says fard is part, sunnah is entire.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position relied upon and what is the mufta bihi?
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: wiping entire head once is sunnah mu'akkadah.

Source Text

(وَ) يسن ( اسْتِيعَابُ الرَّأْسِ بالمَسْحِ)، لما حكت الربيع بنت مسعود « أنها رأت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يتوضأ قالت: فمسح رأسه، ما أقبل منه، وما أدبر وصدغيه وأذنيه مرة واحدة . فلذا قيد المسح بقوله (مَرّةً)، ولتضافر الطرق الصحيحة على مسحه مرة واحدة؛ لإلحاقه بالتيمم والجبيرة ). وحمــل مـا ورد من تثليثه على تحقيق الاستيعاب، وحمل تعدد الماء فيه على قلة البلة، أو نفادها، لا ليكون سنة مستمرة، إذ وضعه على التخفيف بخلاف المضمضة والاستنشاق.
And [the sunnah of] tathlith (washing three times), and [the sunnah of] isti'ab of the head with wiping once... His fingers with water, God will separate them with fire on the Day of Resurrection. And it was not obligatory by the command in His statement: 'My Lord commanded me.' And they did it because of the presence of the deterrent, which is the teaching of the Bedouin, and the absence of mentioning tathlith in what was narrated of his wudu. The manner of tathlith of the fingers of the hands is to insert some into others, and inserting them into flowing water and what is in its ruling suffices. Its description for the feet is to tathlith with the little finger of the left hand the little finger of the right foot first, and end with the little finger of the left foot. This is how it is narrated. Al-Kamal said: 'Allah knows best that it is an accidental matter, not an intended sunnah, so the sunnah of tathlith is not specific to this manner.' And it is sunnah to tathlith al-ghusl (wash three times) – he restricted it to indicate that repeating the wipe is not sunnah, because a man came to the Prophet and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, how is purification?' So he called for water in a vessel, washed his hands three times, then washed his face three times, then washed his forearms three times, then wiped his head, then inserted his two index fingers into his ears, and wiped with his thumbs the outside of his ears and with his index fingers the inside, then washed his feet three times three times, then said: 'This is wudu; whoever adds to this or reduces has done badly and wronged.' In the wording of Ibn Majah: 'has transgressed and wronged.' Al-Nasa'i: 'has done badly, transgressed, and wronged.' That is, if he believes that it is sunnah; doing badly is by adding, and wronging is by reducing. As for if he adds with the intention of wudu upon wudu, or for tranquility of heart when in doubt, or for lack of need, there is no harm. And it is sunnah to isti'ab al-ra's bi al-mash (cover the entire head with wiping), because al-Rabi' bint Mu'awwidh narrated that she saw the Prophet performing wudu; she said: 'He wiped his head, what was in front and what was behind, his temples and his ears, once.' Therefore he restricted the wipe with 'once', and because of the multiplicity of authentic chains for wiping it once; to analogize it with tayammum and the splint. He interpreted what was narrated of wiping three times as for achieving coverage, and interpreted the multiplicity of water in it as due to lack of moisture or its depletion, not to be a continuous sunnah, since his wudu was based on ease, contrary to rinsing the mouth and nose.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains two sunnah acts of wudu: washing each limb three times (tathlith) and wiping the entire head once (isti'ab). The author begins by mentioning the ruling (sunnah) from the matn, then provides proof from the hadith of the Bedouin. The hadith shows the Prophet performed wudu in this manner and declared that adding or reducing is blameworthy. The text also addresses a potential misunderstanding: if one repeats wudu for a legitimate reason (e.g., doubt or extra cleanliness), it is permissible. Then for isti'ab, the proof is from the hadith of al-Rabi' bint Mu'awwidh, and the author explains why wiping once is sunnah, similar to tayammum and splint. The passage concludes by reconciling narrations of wiping three times as being for coverage rather than an independent sunnah.

Key Terms
تثليث الغسل (tathlīth al-ghusl): Washing the limbs three times each in wudu, considered sunnah mu'akkadah.
استيعاب الرأس بالمسح (istiʿāb al-raʾs bi al-masḥ): Wiping the entire head (including ears) once, as sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Tathlith and isti'ab in wudu are sunnah mu'akkadah, based on the hadith of the Bedouin and the practice of the Prophet, and overstepping this is blameworthy unless for a valid reason.

Sunnah of Wiping the Ears in Wudu
Establishes the sunnah of wiping ears and clarifies that it may be done with the water of the head or new water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping ears in wudu and evaluate the evidence for the inter-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
Wiping ears is sunnah; you may use leftover head water or take new water.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on wiping the ears during wudu. It explains that the act is sunnah, not obligatory, and that it is permissible to use the water remaining from wiping the head or to take fresh water. The lesson also addresses the disagreement with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools, who require new water. Understanding this difference ensures correct practice and avoids unnecessary doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its Hanafi ruling
The act is wiping the ears (masḥ al-udhunain). According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah muakkadah. Determine that it is not fard or wajib.
The matn explicitly says 'yusannu' (it is sunnah).
2
Locate the Hanafi evidence
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet wiped his head and ears with one handful. Identify this as the primary dalil.
The hadith is narrated by al-Hakim and others, classified as ahad.
3
State the opposing view and its evidence
Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that new water must be taken for the ears. Their evidence is another narration where the Prophet took separate water for his ears.
Opposing school: Malik and Shafi'i.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the separate-water narration as a case where the moisture from the head had dried. Thus, it does not contradict the general permissibility.
The response is based on reconciling the two narrations.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, a Hanafi may wipe the ears with the same water used for the head. A Shafi'i or Maliki must take fresh water. This affects the performance of wudu in terms of convenience and water usage.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the difference in required action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومسح الأذنين، ولو بماء الرأس، والدَّلْكُ، والولاء، والنية . (۲) (1) (وَ) يسن (مَسْحُ الأُذُنين)، لما رواه الحاكم وغيره، عن ابن عباس ، أنه قال: «ألا أخبركم بوضوء رسول الله ؟ وفيه: ثم غرف غرفة فمسح بها رأسَهُ وأذنيه . وإنما قال: (ولو بماء الرأس). إشارة إلى أنه لو أخذ لهما ماء جديداً مع بقاء البلة، كان حسناً، لما رويناه، فلا يشترط أن يكون بماء الرأس، ولا يشترط له أخذ ماء جديد كما شرطه الإمام مالك والشافعي رحمهما الله، « لأنَّه صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذ لأذنيه ماء خلاف الماء الذي أُخذَ لرأسه » (٣) لأنه حمل على نفاذ البلـة، وتكلموا في كيفيـة مســح الأذنين إذا أراده بماء الرأس والأظهر أنه يضع كفيه وأصابعه على مقدم رأسه، ويمدهما إلى قفاه على وجه يستوعب جميع الرأس، ثم يمسح أذنيه بإصبعيه، ولا يكون الماء مستعملاً بهذا لأن الاستيعاب بماء واحد، لا يكون إلا بهذا الطريق.
And [the sunnah of] wiping the ears, even with the water of the head, and [the sunnah of] rubbing, continuity, and intention. (1)(2) And it is sunnah to wipe the ears, because al-Hakim and others narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Shall I not tell you about the wudu of the Messenger of Allah?' In it: 'Then he scooped a handful and wiped his head and his ears.' And he only said 'even with the water of the head' to indicate that if he takes new water for them while the moisture remains, it is good, as we have narrated. So it is not required that it be with the water of the head, nor is it required to take new water as Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i stipulated, because the Prophet took for his ears water different from the water taken for his head. This is interpreted as the moisture having dried. And they discussed the manner of wiping the ears if one wants to do it with the water of the head. The apparent view is that he places his palms and fingers on the front of his head and extends them to the back in a way that covers the entire head, then wipes his ears with his two fingers, and the water is not considered used because coverage with one handful is only achieved in this way.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage illustrates the Hanafi position on wiping the ears in wudu. It is sunnah to wipe the ears, and it is permissible to use the leftover water from the head or to take fresh water. The author cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet wiped his head and ears with one handful. He then addresses the disagreement with Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i, who require fresh water for the ears. The Hanafi response interprets the narration of the Prophet taking separate water as due to the moisture having dried, thus not contradicting the general permissibility. Finally, the preferred method of wiping ears with head water is described: one wipes the entire head and then the ears with the same handful.

Key Terms
مسح الأذنين (masḥ al-udhunain): Wiping the ears as part of wudu, considered sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if one wipes the ears during wudu, is it required to take new water specifically for the ears?
A) Yes, it is wajib
B) No, it is permissible to use the water from the head
C) It is fard to take new water
D) It is makruh to use the head water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wiping ears with the water from the head, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas, while Shafi'i and Maliki require new water.
